O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, most dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its content, and I have made an end to it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I would complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is entirely estranged from everything else, so that the science has perished and been lost, and nothing remains of it except the small descriptions in books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I will revive it together with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will also come together with the forms of cautery bandages and the other instruments of the work along with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation for it, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for whoever undertakes this to be well-versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so long as he knows the joints of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and blood vessels, and the number of them, and their movements and rest, and from where they issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason does Hippocrates say that a name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We warn you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously said, should beware lest they err and harm people; thus have I often warned many of those who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut off i.e. amputated the neck of a woman with scrofula or a goiter, and he cut the arteries of the neck; why so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another surgeon who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they were to remove it, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I have seen another surgeon who took on the treatment of a duke from our land, who had his leg broken and with the break was also wounded. And the ignorant surgeon tightened the splint over the wound with a strong bandage, and did not leave any space for ointment, and left it thus until the end; and he commanded that it should not be loosened, and thus the duke's leg remained as it was, all inflamed and putrid, and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to loosen the leg splint; and when I loosened it, he felt at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But despite everything, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire limb had been lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another surgeon who opened up an infected abscess, and then inflamed it further through his malpractice.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the chancre, when it is free of melancholic humour, one must not touch it with iron if it is not in a place where everything that is corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, most excellent son, it is necessary for you to know that manual work is divided into two parts: namely, the work where there is danger in several conditions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Why it is necessary that you keep them for yourselves, so that the foolish people cannot speak ill of you. If you take up arms in confidence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave the fearful diseases to have a grave outcome; and remove from yourselves those things that cause doubt, and be steadfast in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take lightly to treat a bad disease, lest you be called foolish physicians.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterizing with fire and about medical cautery, and it is the chapter ordered from head to toe; and about the forms of instruments and the handles of the cauterizer, and about everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about poultices and wounds, and about extracting splinters, and similar things; and it is the chapter ordered with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to toe, with the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say what quality of aid and of harm each constitution has.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest and most subtle science, with secret responses; and many wise people have spoken about it and agreed on this point; and they spared themselves from saying more because I was afraid to lengthen out my words.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterizing always helps all constitutions where there is matter, except for two: that is to say, the hot constitution with matter, and the dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry constitution together with matter, some people said that cauterizing is a great aid; and others said the opposite: that cauterizing is of no use for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	Because the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured by heat or dryness itself. And those who said the opposite said that cauterizing makes a great aid for hot and dry illnesses that come into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	Because when you compare the body of a man to its moisture and to the temperature of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true some time through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should meddle with this except the person who has tried it out and knows through long experience the chapter of cauterizing, and the diversity of human constitutions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the remedies and the urgency of the moment; as for other constitutions, we have no fear of them, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all physicians assembled and agreed on cauterizing.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterizing with fire is a secret of the cures, and more excellent virtue than cauterizing with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come into the other member unless it has been cooked, and it harms no other member if its name is known.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot remedies come from member to member by loosening, and bring diseases with serious outcome to the affected member; and perhaps kill the patient. The fires because of their great strength and the goodness of their substance do not do so, if there is no surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this to be true by experiment and through the length of my service and study which I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things. And for that reason I excuse myself from the length of this speech, because I do not like to deprive you of the secret that is known as fire, and the quality of its work, how it cures illnesses in the body, just as the philosopher says in demonstrating it; accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizing should be done, and chose suitable patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterizing is suitable at any time, because the remedies for the harm are placed under the aid of cauterizing; and indeed if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for a more serious illness to come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for the illness that is cured by cauterizing does not have a relapse; and they say so themselves. But it's not like they think, because cauterizing is only medicine that changes the complexion, dries out the humors that are the cause of the pain, and its value lies in its speed, virtue of its work, and lordship over the patient.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it's possible that the illness comes back sometimes according to the complexion of the sick person and the location of the illness and its nature; and all the superfluities are gathered in him through the acquisition of rich foods and similar things, unless he is given cauterizations at the place where there is too much superfluity and moisture, such as dens for pain and similar things, and that kind of pain does not return. But this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people don't understand why cauterizing is called the last resort of medicine, and that's true; but they think it's only used when other treatments fail, not recognizing that cauterizing can be effective even when other remedies have failed. Their intention is wrong, and cauterizing is indeed the last resort of medicine because when we administer various cures for any illness and they don't work, then we use cauterizing, and it's worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	So now it is clear that cauterizing is the last resort of medicine, not as foolish doctors intend.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizing with instruments of gold is more effective than those made of iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They also said that the place where the cauterization takes effect does not cause corruption, but it's not true, for I have tested it and found that in some people, it is indeed true; and cauterizing with gold is more effective than iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And in any case, when you heat an instrument of gold, you don't know when it's hot enough because of the color of the gold, and it cools down right away. And if you heat it too much, it melts; so there are many obstacles to consider.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of this, we use instruments made of iron for cauterizing, which we have found suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter according to its main point from start to finish, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Of olive cauterizing (or olive oil cauterization).
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This olive cauterizing is effective against moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types: one that is used to treat a disease called "soda", and another due to many humors that descend from the head to the ears; also for a multitude of dreams and pains in the dens (temples), and pain in the throat, and especially against all diseases caused by coldness such as paralysis, stroke, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this olive cauterizing is that the sick person be purged with a solvent medicine that clears the head, three or four times, as the virtues and age and habituation of the sick person can tolerate. And then redress the head of the sick person.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on the balance. Next, place the root of your palm over the root of his nose, between his two eyes; and let the heat come from your middle fingers, if it bleeds, then apply the olive cauterizing instrument, which is called "olivare", in this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and move your hand down and outwards in a slow circular motion, then lift your hand suddenly, and reward yourself if you see the bone 1 small sol; and if you don't see it, repeat the cauterizing until you see the bone as I told you. After that, take 1 spoonful of wool, and place it in a warm compress with soft cotton inside, and apply it to the spot, and leave it for 3 days; after that, apply a moistened cotton ball in butter, and leave it on until the heat is gone; then cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacion" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancient ones said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges, and because of this, it is a greater aid.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that you should cauterize so much that part of the bone is burned, and then resorb what has been burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that you should cauterize so much on top and press it so hard that the bone is lowered as wide as 1 vertole (a type of strip) that women put in their hair, because the humors are thus expelled; and the wound should be left open for a long time; after that, it should be cured and closed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And I do not think that these two ways of cauterizing are good in all cases, except for those who have a way out through fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them alone. For the eyes are weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we observe in other members; and similarly, when the eyes of the sick person are weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterizing is more salutary and effective for me, and with this method I have been working until now to assemble salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the head suffers from chronic pain and lasts for a long time, the sick person should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purging of the head and oils and plasters. And if they are given the cauterizing that we have spoken of before, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take note if the eyes of the sick person are naturally strong and not too cold; then cauterize under that with a small amount of what we said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Then make cauterizing on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and make one cauterization at the spot called "vasselz"; it is a place where one puts venesections. And hold your hand so that you don't see up to the bone: the sick person feels a much greater pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than those for the middle part of the head. This is the form.
dou cautere dou chief	Of the cauterizing of the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in some part of the head comes sudden pain, and the disease is spread up to the eye, and the skull is purged by medicinal means and one has done all the other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases, and none of this helps: then make fire cauterization by two methods, namely with a cold remedy and with heat.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cauterization of cold remedy is that you take a lump of alum, and remove the rind and recast it into one vessel as two eyes, and then make an incision in the temple where the pain lies in such a way that you can put the lump of alum under the skin; and when it is replaced, bind and tighten it well and leave it so for twelve hours; and then unbind and treat further the lump of alum, and leave the wound so for two or three days; then put on a cotton poultice in butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment cure as long as it is healed; and if you see that make those from some burning medicines that I have written or secondly to treat burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery to such a heat, that this be its shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a clover with a small lump in the middle. And it has a small appearance; and you put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly until the center of the burning point is red-hot; and lift your hand so that the arteries don't burn, which are further away, and there is an abundance of blood flowing.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Then you put cotton on top of the silk and leave it on for three days; then I put damp cotton in beeswax, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with a cautery called "cultellare", do so at the tip, and be careful not to touch the artery in the migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure the headache as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned from medicine and iron do not help, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign over the painful place a line half a finger's length long, and withdraw your hand once, and ensure that you do not touch the artery and get only as far as the bone; and be careful of the jaw which moves when eating, and the nerves have regard for it so that spasms do not come to the patient, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or a great fear comes and especially to him who does not know himself, and who is not an expert; and leave the work to myself. But I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you at the place where it hurts in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the area on the head in the same way as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with a cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	This phrase appears to be a medieval medical diagnosis or description of a condition.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from the ear due to coldness, and one has worked with dissolvent medicines and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pains do not subside, then warm this cautery which is called "point", by which I mean the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After point the entire area around the ailing ear, or around both sides where the pain is located in both, and move away about a little above the root of the ear since you have marked the place to be incised; and apply 10 points around each ear; after cure the spot until it becomes sound.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cautery is only those which move due to phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar symptoms that come from heat and vomit of bile.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this appearance of torture that moves due to yellow phlegm and purgations of the head and gurgling, and it doesn't work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the ailing area with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another about a little behind the temple, and the third in the meeting of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery on the head of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger; and leave the cautery so high up that the middle of the cure is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the cutlery that we have placed earlier, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the knife be a little larger; after that, cure the spot as I said before, until it becomes sound.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in the same way as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then they make four cauteries: two on the horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the spot called "vasselz" as we said earlier, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and cure them as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this sickness, it is necessary to give the patient great years and pills that purify the brain; after which one washes the head of the sick person thoroughly, and puts on the occiput a poultice of mustard written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: if one does it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is cured thus, it is well; and if not, one makes him three cauterizations below the head as far as the neck, and has space of two inches between each cautery; and cures it in the same manner as the others, and if you see that it is swelling and the patient is suffering, one makes a cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others above the two horns, and cures until he is cured; and this cautery which is called "olivare", just as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and with what we have said before; after which one washes the head of the sick person, then makes a cautery in the head and on each horn, and one behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the sickness is severe, one makes four cauterizations above the spine of the back; and leaves it until the most painful part is burned, and lifts your hand; after which one cures him until he is cured, and this is the cautery which is called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	The epilepsy (note: the Middle English word used here is likely a precursor to modern French "maladie d'épilepsie", rather than a direct translation)
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cautery unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to purify the brain with years and other treatments that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffers from severe pain.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if this is a child who cannot hold their breath, have them gargle and chew on something that makes the head clear frequently with good meats; after which pour oil into the head in a cloth, and do one fire cautery as we have said before, and one fire cautery above the jawbone, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and suffering, do cauteries as I have said to that person who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and be the cauteries olive as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is infantile, make him one i.e. a subtle fire cauterization in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or corrupt and moist humors are thickened, then make him the fire cauterization that we said to do to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities decline towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then make him drink something by which the brain may be cleansed, as it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heat the head of the patient; afterwards make one linen cloth well made, also like a circle, and put it on his head; and the patient should be crossed over, and held tightly from all sides; then apply the liniment, and worth full measure of old balm; and warm him to temperate fire, so that the drink may go in which he can bear; afterwards empty the ring within his head, and let it cool down; and do this for the patient once a week each time with good government, until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize someone by making many points all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cauterizing moistens the brain equally; and then put on wet cotton in butter and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	This appears to be the end of the text, and "de l'awe des eulz" is likely a phrase indicating that the recipe or instructions are finished, with "l'awe" being an old-fashioned word for "law" or "rule", and "des eulz" meaning "of them" or "of these things". So, it's a way of saying "the end" or "the conclusion".
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the first symptom appears of these things by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and make the patient drink something cleansing the head, and keep him from all moisture, and let him sweat or take several baths on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding the patient to raise his head, and making him a fire cautery on the head, and making two cauterizations on the two temples if the descending of the abscess is at both eyes together, or in one place if it is in one; and close all the veins and arteries that are under the scalp, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and beware of bleeding, and if you see a lot of blood coming out, stop it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to stop the bleeding, and never do a cautery or incision below both bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	under the eye sockets
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of both eyes are old and accustomed, and are above the veins, or near the arteries that appear on the surface of the head outside; and one sees that it is a cold, slimy superfluity, then he makes the cautery that I said at the beginning of the abscess descending to the eyes: one cautery in the head, and two cauterizations above both temples, and two cauterizations or incisions below both bones; and if there is need for more, so he cauterizes sharply on the crown all over small cauters.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from within the eye sockets (or eyeballs)
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit at all, then give him to drink three times a day of bad wine; after that put oil on his head, and make a cautery with olive oil; and do two cauterizations of the cautery called "clavilis" above both crowns, one close to the ears; and beware of the artery so you don't cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	to such a form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that they make two fire cauterizations on the two moles so long as the moles are; and do not leave the hand until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	two hairs which prick the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyelids become converted into thorns, and prick the eye, and then one makes a cauterization according to two manners: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the fire cauterization orders the sick person to leave the hairs until they are long and equal; and if they prick at their birth, then one binds the eyelids so that they do not move until they have grown.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are equal, then the sick person places a bandage on his eye; afterwards he writes on paper of the eyelids a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and is the beginning of the sign below the hairs; then he puts moistened cotton in egg white and muskallonge juice of persimmon on the eye, then he heats the cauterization with which this is its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have drawn with small points and strokes many times, so that the scar is burned in place; and the sign of the health of the eye is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the scalding is gone; afterwards cure with ointment until it is sound.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come and the paper is softened then recommence the cauterization on the very same, just as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural height, and is equal, and does not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medicine cauterization is that you command the sick person to leave the hairs as long as they are great and equal, then make parchment the shape of the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and live coal, each a third part, and grind them together well; and do it hastily, so that it does not cool down. Then spread it on the shape you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it under the eyelids; and if the sickness is in one eye only, then work on one, and if also in both, then work on both. And put cotton moistened in egg white under the eye, and the sick person's tears should be in a bandage and you place your finger showing on the medicine, and press once or twice every time the sick person feels stinging from the medicine, because it stings like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have made them long, take the medicine at your due time.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the blister has passed away, then lift up the scab and see if you notice the parchment lifted in the same way as if it had been lifted by constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then place medicine again on the place where the medicine had effect, so that your work is equal and your eyes are set in place; then put on wet cotton wool in a shell until the hot places have cooled down; afterwards cure the place with ointment which is called "dyafenis" and others until it is sound.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to take good care of your work with great care, so that the medicine does not fall into your eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the eye, then put medicine again on that place which is softened with clean paper properly, thus as you have done before; after that cure it until it is sound; and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the humors of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to these be thy contraindications; and do not think that the right way is shown to him who has the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	It appears to be a medieval medical text, specifically a section on treating fistulas (abnormal connections or passageways between two body parts) using cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit at all, then it is necessary that you make a fire cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put their head into your hand; and have a servant hold their head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or turn its head. After this, place damp cotton on top of an egg yolk or persimmon juice over the eye; after that heat up the cautery until it is like the shape of a hen's feather, along with the handle being the cautery itself. If you wish, make it pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, also as wide as a tent; but however, what is shaped in this way will be worth your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and remove the dirt, and dry it; and if it is closed, work on it, and remove the pus from it. After that place the hot cautery shape over it, and hold your hand with the cautery at the part near the eye so that your hands do not make a mistake; and put the cautery into the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization right up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then repeat the cautery one more time, and another if necessary, and let it be for three days. Then put on moistened cotton in a burrow, and apply an unguent drying treatment until they are healed, and if forty days pass without healing, put on corrosive medicine of water until the bone is revealed; and dress according to what he comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand as a fistula, and cut out the place; afterwards put in the incision a subtle caiman's skin or what is its form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make the quantity of an ounce of poultice; and hold your hand or camahan firmly, and do not move the patient's eyes until the poultice is set in place; and it is necessary to put a moistened cotton swab over the eye of the patient: if the poultice does settle into a fistula, and the wound has become wonderfully healthy.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer a perforation to the navel, and bring back the fistula to its own place in the navel according to what is proper for itself.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times these cracks in the lips are called "pox", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it immediately into those cracks as long as it will fit; afterwards, apply oil to the place until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the tonsils or on the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after it has made a hole and has become swollen and turned into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have one cauterizing iron according to the size of the fistula; afterwards put the bottom or poultice of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron becomes hot at the point of it, and on the last place; and do this once or twice, afterwards treat it with what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	of the disease of the teeth (likely referring to dental abscess or tooth decay)
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and they don't work, then put the patient's head in your healthy one; afterwards heat up the cauterizing iron whose form will come forth like this: place a cane on the tooth; and put hot iron inside immediately, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards lift your hand and reheat the cauterizing iron according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and let them spit it out once an hour for a long time.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is consolidated, and the softened gums are tightened, and the moisture that had corrupted is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth (likely referring to toothache)
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold or there is cold or warmth inside, and the remedies of medicine don't work, then it's necessary to cauterize in two ways: with butter cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cauterization is done in this way: you take a piece of goat butter and shape it into a iron spoon or a bronze one; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and melt it in hot butter, and put it on the painful tooth immediately and hold it until it cools down; and do so often until its virtues come to the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton are wet with cold butter, put them on the painful tooth, and then place a hot iron until the fire reaches the apex of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery consists of taking a cauldron of iron or lead, and it should be large so that the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient. After this, heat the cautery until it takes shape, and then place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be removed on the same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter in the act of placing that cautery, and then let it cool down; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery wherever you wish, and according to what power you have; and this is the form of the cord:
des scrophules	Of the scrofulas.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of a damp and cold nature, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery that will take shape as follows, and have two openings for the fumes to come out from the other side; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the core of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery according to its size, and leave it like that for three days; and put on moistened cotton in butter until the inflammation is removed; afterwards cure the place with ointments and poultices until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the body:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures conquer on the channels of the body, and similarly when it comes from cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with soluble medicines; after which do cautery at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not come up to the throat, and burn only as much as a hazelnut.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that do another cautery at the joint of the neck at the tip of the spine, and let the cauteries be called "clavicules" as we have shown before; and treat the place so as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	The treatment for scrofula (tuberculosis) seems to be quite... primitive, compared to modern medical standards.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every disease of pormon are from cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or sweat, and the illness is old, then make two cauteries on the scrotum in the middle; and one other cautery in between the nipples, and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be according to the form that was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, do a cauterization by piercing entirely the cauter that is called "points" as the shape is shown before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to thirty or thereabout.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After the cure has been made according to what is said before, and the cautery should be at three inches according to this form.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that the cauteres are lighter, because you make three in one stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the joint of the shoulder is dislocated because of moisture, and one puts it back in place, and it cannot stay but rather goes out again and becomes dislocated with a little movement that happens, as we have proven, then it is necessary that you reinsert the first dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Then have the patient sit down on their back and on their chest; then lift up the kettle that is inside the blister with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, then heat up the cautery which has two handles of double iron (this is the form):
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the kettle as long as it penetrates to the chest, and the fluid of the cautery will come together in 4 cavities; and that is why the cautery is made with the cautery which has 3 handles, because the figure of cauterization are 6 cavities; and they are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and that is the form of the cautery which has 3 handles:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And at no time are the threads attached to this one nerve for which there are .viii. (8) cavities.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards place the cautery on the body and wrap it with cloth; afterwards have the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, that same thing happens again, then make a cautery above the thick part of the cautery peg, or many cauterizations in piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is refixed, and the moisture is eliminated, and the patient's wound is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold humors and much moisture come into the stomach and they pull him away from his complexion, and many ulcers form in him, and by the usual modes of cure he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on their back, and stretch out their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Then make three cauterizations one below the edge of the rib per the size of an egg, with a whole cautery peg, and two cauterizations outside on both sides so that the shape of the cauterizations is at three angles, and there be such space between the one and the other that they are not joined together when they will spit pus; and be the cauterizations so deep that they pierce the two parts of the bone, and the shape of the cauterizations should be according to this form without joining.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see the need to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach at the point according to the quantity that you see from the instrument; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the cure that we have had before, as long as it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes to pain from cold and moisture and from thick windiness, as long as it is very foully changed from its natural complexion through superfluities; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit them, then the patient should be put on their stomach; and sign with an instrument III cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, below the hypochondriac region, there where the breast comes from; and let there be space between each cautery the size of a thumb; and may the cauteries be as long as the length of the body, and do not press too hard with your hand all over the cautery; and only burn the outer half of it; and the patient should be straight on their feet; and if they cannot, then let them lean back, stretch out their legs, and lift up their arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your will is so, then cauterize these cauteries with the cutellary, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn too much of the flesh; for you would dry out all the body; and it should not come just to boiling, for the flesh is very subtle there, and you know this for sure.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels great pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when the cure of the mirrors is finished, it is necessary that the patient be covered on his head; and then sign to have a place marked where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterer which is similar to the sun, because this is its shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I the cautery so that the burns be done, and come just to suppurate, so that the pustule be completely drained; after the cure according to the treatment of boils until it is healed; and there is no need for anyone to use this cautery who has not studied medicine long and by whose hands these diseases have cured at any time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly work, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	from the cautery of pustules (a type of blister or abscess)
