Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must make pustule cauterizers from the roots of aristologia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristologia as large as you can find, and let it be dry, and also as thick and as long as your arm; and dip it in oil, and hold it in the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauterizers a little lower down on the part that is under the beard; and two cauterizers between the fifth rib and the lowest one, sloping back a little; and one cautery in the breast, and another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two below the two ribs behind the cautery that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand hard, but rather hold it openly like when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And said one old man that some person uses the fire cautery similar to the rasp, and heats it up and puts it between their ribs, until it comes to that abscess; and the pain bursts forth like we have said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient will die now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (possibly a reference to a medical instrument or tool)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse in the manner that we have said in the sections on cures, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of cauterization that are good for all:
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of the one manner, thus is that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a line following the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cauterization that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and be sure the patient sits over his back; and another manner of cauterization is that you heat the cauterization which has two handles, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the handle which is next to the mouse, or where the patient's rib comes towards the left, and be the elevation from which you lift the handle according to the handle, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Then you put the two handles ablaze so that the handle is felt from the other side, and then pull out the cauterization, and thus there will be four of them. And if you see this, then cauterize the entire cauterization with three handles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the cure when he has gotten pus for a long time, and this is worth less than the other remedies previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	The cautery is not worth anything to an edema, except for the manner which is called "scalding".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make IV cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and II behind the back on the spine, and I near the point of the breast; and let the cauterizations be very close to the skin.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, let the cautery be open and allow it to drain for a long time until purulence is gone, and do not stop the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and recovery would hasten, and the two intentions ( possibly a reference to the cauterization and the disease) would be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the key that we have shown before; and those for the back are olive-shaped, according to what has been described earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling (or inflammation) of the feet (possibly a reference to a medical condition or disease affecting the lower limbs)
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who is edematous, and are full of yellowish fluid, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep within; thus the cauter should burn the area around the yellowish boil, and be the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make two cauterizers on each leg, one at the tip of the little finger; and the cauterizers should be long, one under the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg. Let the cauterizers stay open for a long time without treating until the yellowish fluid comes out, then treat with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the blistering
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the belly is inflamed due to cold and moisture, so much that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are dulled, and cannot be cured by any remedies; and you see the patient very suffering and of great strength, then make a large cautery over the stomach as has been spoken of before or the belly cautery, to the circulatory cautery; and four small cauterizations around the mouth subtle so that every one is like a single subtle cautery, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then make a cautery over the elbow, and one cautery over each shoulder blade, and two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large one, because the treatment is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or more, and are old and of cold, moist, corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not help, make a cautery: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind the almacote patch and patch in triangulating, and I cautery under the jaw, II to be done; and if you think that the stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and we see the face swell, then make a great cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery pointed; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure has fixed the place until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshiness which is called "the lump"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut off the lump, if you heat the cauter that looks like a razor, and then put it completely on fire over that lump which is being cut off; and leave your hand there until the cauter reaches the navel, so the wound will close quickly. Do this once or twice, and if there's a lot of lumpiness, then cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat them with ointments to cure them as long as they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cauter on the armpit, it will cause more harm.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the sick person cannot endure cutting or an opening, which we will tell about in its place, there comes that disease that cannot be healed except by cauterizing.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a boil comes and is festering and discharges foul-smelling corrupt moisture, then you should carefully test it to its full depth, and make sure that you know how deep it has penetrated.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which seems very hot, and put it into the boil according to the depth that the tent has entered, and reheat the cautery as long as those foul and corrupt flesh are burned once, or twice, or three times, depending on how great the need is; and be careful not to burn the nerves which are nearby, and do not burn too many veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the boil goes to the bladder and to the intestines, then be careful of those places, and do not apply fire to them unless it is in a fatty area, and think that it is not a plague; after curing the place until it is healed, and if the ulcer is closed, and the materials are removed for a long time, then know that the ulcer is entirely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the ulcer is thickened and corrupts the bone to its core; and thus as one of those which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys and they are swollen and not menstruating, then it is necessary that you cauterize them with a cauter on one side and on the other with a cauter with a claw, which we have spoken of before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three caters in line, and they will make greater help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the sick person retains urine, then you should cauterize in the area above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one to the right and one to the left, and each of them should be as long as a finger's breadth; and you should make one cauter behind the back, or two if needed; and the caters should be claw-like, according to the form previously mentioned.
de la marris	of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow conception to occur, and the flowers (i.e. menstrual blood) are corrupted and delayed, and when they come, there is a great pain: then it is necessary to make three caters around the belly, as we have said about the cauter of the bladder, and two caters behind the back; and the caters should be claw-like, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the navel (or belly button)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the navel (or belly button) and because of this cause it moves away from its place, and the sign is that the hip is longer than the other when measured together; and if you find the root of the departure of the intestines nearby, then you should cauterize the sick person on the navel's area with one cauter in the shape of a circle, and mark it before the place around the navel as it turns, so that the navel is inside the circle; and the cauter should be like those by which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauters are not present, then make three large cauters of olive stone (i.e. a type of iron) and the cauters should be as deep as all the others; and cure until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the navel (or belly button)
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the back of the thigh, and it is caused by coldness and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure is not worth anything, and the disease is ancient: then you must purify the patient from the thick humors with foul pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is thus: namely by applying hot medicines together, and by cauterizing with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is done in many ways, one of which is: that you cauterize on the hip bone three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make them deep and broad, and have space between each cautery the size of an egg, and be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on top of the hip bone, for which there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterization is on the circular cautery that we have said before in the dislocation of the thigh; but make it in such a way that the circle contains all the thigh, and all the tendons of the knee are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which one does it for sciatica, when the pain remains in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then one makes two cauteries there where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery four fingerbreadths above the ankle, on the left side a little; and be knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the iron burn; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as three or four fingers' breadth from the foot or near the knee, then cauterize where he feels the pain three or four points, or what is called "point cautery".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, I make more; and if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then I make a cautery with a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauterizations not to burn too little so as to spare the nerves and large arteries, and not to cause the patient greater nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have had a fire cautery on the heel of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet as well, and was pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purgation by belly which caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, do a cautery on one and the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said in the cautery of the groin, about this is the manner, make such an iron and be as thick at the top as a nutshell of date, or one penny less, and be between two holes and be from one end to the other the length of a hazelnut seed; and be the holes as wide as two fingers, and also like nuts, and have a good made manchon (iron) of iron; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated thoroughly until it is entirely red and hot; then place it on the wooden board of the sick person, and turn it over on the healthy side; and cauterize once .i. cautery repeated and let it leave .iij. days; and then make a poultice of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use the pot of this cauterizer for fear of his glance, and see how many people use it; and nonetheless it is a good cauterizer which can be endured, and where it applies.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The instruments for the burning cautery of medicine are those made between two handles where the edge of the door descends, and they should be of brass or iron with a long handle, and in the height have 2 nails, and between each one the quantity of the thickness of an egg; and be open at the front and back, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Put the wooden handle of the cautery on the patient lying on their side with their healthy side uppermost, and press your hand strongly on the handle of the cautery; then cast between the two circles of hot water which has been heated over the fire in a pot, and let it stay for one hour of time, and allow the patient to feel the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it finds a burn there as well from the fire; and when the burn has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and lift the wooden handle away from the sweet water, and let it be so for three days, and put on ointment until what is black from the scalding is removed; and let it be for three days that the purging goes out; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments until they are healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread all the way to the thigh or all the way to the leg, then make the instrument that you use again according to what you have done in the hip similarly; and this is the method of applying heat, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and quicklime, as much from one as from the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new cauldron.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where there is a small hole at the back so that the point of a knife can fit in; and put on top of that cauldron another cauldron well weighted down, and put on top alkaline and quicklime and sweet heat above, until it has gone into the two powders so that you will have enough to soak your hand; and leave it like that until the hot clear broth and residue descend into the leaded cauldron; then take all that broth, and pour it onto the quicklime and alkaline just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very severe and is to be administered with various medical works and cauteries of other members For it does a great work like fire, and if well cauterized with linseed oil, honey, anacardium, and wax with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one man was cured of the pain of the back and sciatic vein, and he greatly praises it, and says that no other cure was made, and that he was healed at once when this treatment was done, and he bathed himself as he teaches hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take fresh and dry verdigris green, and grind it very well with a pea of fat, and apply it on the back and on the thigh and on the leg or where the pain is held, and tie it; and let it be for three hours and by as much as the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into a bath until his body is somewhat warmed up, and put him in bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	Know that no one should use cauterization with such medications, unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's hair, it greatly helps; and the cauters should be made in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and butter it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other one which is called a fossicle.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry goat's hair and set it on fire until it is charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let it stay until it cools down; and do it again in this way, and do not cease doing so until you think by sense that it will come up to the navel, and that the pain will cease; and this manner of cauterization is called "cautery of goat's hair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or concussion or from too great evacuation, or from appearance of cold matter spread, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from infusing cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after that, the sick person to be voided of fetid pills or other similar things, so that on their back, where the pain lies, three lines are marked with ink, and in each line 5 cauterizers or more according to virtue and quantity that the sick person can endure; and the cauterizers shall be made according to the cauterizer called "point"; and if you wish, make 3 cauterizers or 4 at the middle nail-like according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have tight hiccups when they laugh, and fear; and you find in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance that comes on top of the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, then cauterize at the point of the "poins" according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So instruct the patient to apply a red cautery equally to each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see fit, apply a cautery around the spine at a point that is 2 lines or 3 deep, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let the place be soothed until it is completely healed, according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply a cautery in suppurative inflammation which is in danger of nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of joints is due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which the people call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, so it is cured by cauterizing in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-sized according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it becomes necessary that you apply on the face of the foot, then make a cautery all over the cautery which we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and in other joints, and such things happen many times, then make a cautery on each kneecap 3 or 4 times from each part, all over the olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand farther than until the fat of the joint is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend as far as the knee and to the back, administer the cauterization that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the knuckle two lines; and if there remains no pain at all, make points above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come as far as the ribs or as far as the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good government of the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sphincter anus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When swelling comes in the groin, and the testicles descend to the scrotum and this is new, it is necessary that when you see this cured, do not touch him at all that day; and he should use things that ease the belly, so that the wind descends from his belly; then have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to lift up his testicles as long as the swelling is repaired, and then reattach them to their place, and sign over the incision below the swelling on the bone of the elbow, and make a mark that is like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in which there is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and emits pustules.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the intestines to their place; and the servants anoint his hand so that they do not return backward; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put a cushion and a servant under the thighs, and another under the chest which holds his hands; then put the cauterizer on the sign above all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it the first time, repeat it again once until you go up to the bone; and be careful subtly that the pustules do not burst when you do the cauterization; so that you do not burn him; and by this the patient does not die, or other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their size, and for grown people also large according to theirs; after III days cure the place of the cautery with butter so that the scorching is removed; afterwards cure other ointments until they are healed, and have the patient lie on his back for XL days so that the wound is well sewn up; and it is necessary that their swellings be allowed to last a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he will get up in bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after XL days, when he will want to get up, have him put on a well-made bandage and wear it for XL other days; and have good rest, that he not strain himself too much and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of loud shouting; and when he does this instruction then he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the twisting of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come to other areas and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, make the fire cautery of the cautery burn in proportion to its size, and let it be charred with the third part of the core; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but mark the first place of the navel and make a line across the width above the ulcer, and another one below it, and hold your hand in the middle all the way around the whole cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauters are lighter and moister.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, either from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and let the cautery according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of knots and of pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat the other cautery over him, for that custom is that it should move to the member that is closest, therefore you must make the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	De meselerie ( likely a medical or surgical procedure)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The swellings are helped by cauterization at times with great ease, and likewise the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you not see it being cauterized? Take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not leave any residue, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauterizations on the head: one within the head, now deep, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and two above the horns, and one behind on the occipital; and hold your hand so that the cautery comes up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can exit; and cauterize on the nose according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered everywhere and it is clearly worsening, it is necessary that you cauterize with these fires on the head that we have said, and one fire near the navel, and two fires on the spine of the neck, and six fires on the spine of the back, and one large on the hip and one other below, and two on the shoulders; and two on the sides, and two on the tendons of the thigh, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the backside that you do not burn them; and never make a fire on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I do with cauterization, the more it helps the patient, and benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization as much as the healthy person feels it, because their body is already quite corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be that the cauterization is great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in manners of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the treatment, fill the wound with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When an inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then make a cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be one point entering into the flesh of the bone; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at any time one does a cautery and on the hand and foot and back, at the issue of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and nevertheless no one interferes unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the issues of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulcer" is inflamed, and no medicine can help it, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of fat in the skin, until the white spot is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of barley flour and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and vinegar of gall and vinegar of almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and apply it to the wound as long as it is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	Here's how to cure syphilis (chancre) by cauterization:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a carbuncle comes at the beginning, and you look at it carefully, if you cauterize with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the tour of the carbuncle.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise men say that one also makes a cautery in the middle of the carbuncle; and yet it does not seem to me good, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen once; and it is more proper that it be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the inflammation which cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some have an illness that is called "adubelati", and it delays death because of the superfluity that it causes, or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has a flow of blood, or because of the weather; and you see it hasten towards death: then cauterize around them with many small cauteries that prick; afterwards let him be so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through the cauterization, then heat the cauterization until its form melts:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the center, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them externally in such a way that the course of the ulceration is made plain.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards heal him until he is perfectly sound.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure by iron with fire
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of disease is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the member, for it eats up the members just as fire burns dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can suffer fire cautery together, then heat the cauteries with small and large claws, according to what is necessary for the place where the illness is; after cauterizing all around until you have removed all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let him rest for 3 days, and apply oil to the places that have been cauterized until the blisters from the fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of ointments an abscess forms.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after 3 days that a healthy abscess does not form, it is good; and if this does not happen, then resume the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this remedy is sometimes been cured with medicinal poultice in place of fire cauterization; but nevertheless fire cauterization is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medicinal poultice in the division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From boils which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often happens that between the toes appears a disease called "claw" according to our intention, and it is a thick massed thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery of this disease is in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cautery, and water hot cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the cautery iron also like a quill pen, and it be made of good iron to the measure that it can pierce the growth from all sides, and that there are subtle edges; afterwards put it completely hot on the growth, and turn your hand around the growth as much as it goes into the depth of the growth; and leave it thus for three days until it starts to let go of purulence; then make an ointment of bitter mallows boiled with oil, and leave the ointment over all night, and the growth will fall and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment, applying salve until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted by a boil on the body, and often happens in hands and feet, then you should bring a hot iron cautery to bear on it. And do in this manner: take an iron or lead ring, or a point of copper, and put it on the thorn and the nodule, that is to say for warts; and put the ring over so that it touches all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the ring reaches the root of the thorn, and you can let the hot water penetrate deeply right up to the root; and suffer the patient to feel the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will deracinate entirely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So make one like another, until you have extracted all those that are within the body, then treat them with ointments that foster flesh.
li cure dou trembler	It seems like there's a new text snippet provided.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some person trembles with cold or quartan fever or another thing, it is necessary that you make four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; then he will let him shake, and quickly the health will depart from the disease of cold.
des pustules puans	boils that burst.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Any time purulent swellings or pus-filled pustules appear on the surface of the body, which come from corrupted great substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary to do a first treatment when they appear, that one makes a cauterization on the head of each pustule: a subtle cauterization with a stick of myrtle wood, in which the point should be grasped by fire, or with a long aristologia root, or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And any time one cauterizes them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further forward, but the superfluous things from which they come are broken down, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often great discharges of blood come from the artery that is cut in the wound, or from the incision of the abscess, or from the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop them.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your finger's tip on the wound of the vein, and press down as much as the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips out; then put multiple small and large olive cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either great or small according to the wound and its place where the artery runs, and place the cautery on that vein which you hold with your finger, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts out again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, then take promptly another of the cauters that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these one after the other until the bleeding is stopped. And beware that you do not burn the nerve that lies nearby, and that no other malice comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it can not be well stopped in itself, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four ways that we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not tied, or by a strong ligature with thread, or by medicines applied to which have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever reminds them of the dangers of tightly tying with a cloth or putting hot things on them, or other similar things, if they do not benefit them. (This sentence seems to be an aside, possibly written by a different author or added as a note.)
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a surgeon or medicine present, they should put their finger's tip on the wound of the vein as we said, and press down well until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the hand, but moisten it with cold water often until it is very cold so that the bleeding is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make inquiries in advance for the cauters and medicines that they need.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all disease wherein it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or hot medicine, and the reasons and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I put that chapter at the head until now, and I shall go into this chapter by the same way so that what you want to find will be more easily found.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauteries, and therefore it is necessary to be more careful.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Because in the work of this chapter there are many times evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and to the incision above an abscess, and to the care of wounds, and to the extraction of arrows, and to the incision above a bone, and similar things; or there is doubt and fear, and death comes to many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come to be treated.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from those who have so with their illness that they die lightly for the foolishness that they find in their disease, and from the great extent of their wickedness; and one should be afraid of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their mind, and say: "Wait, I am well"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more account in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely with those of whom you are certain, and with whom you can take and hold advantage; and use prognosis and indication in the treatments of your patients for whose salvation it will be converted; and this will help you to achieve good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	And I have ordered this chapter by chapters, dividing according to the chapter of burns, which I have divided from head to foot, for you will find it more easily that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	two full waterheads
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes often to children at birth, and when the cord tightens too strongly around the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur in anyone but children, and with all those that I have seen it has been the cause of death; and for this reason it seems to me that it is not worth my while to continue working on these remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child whose ears were full of water, and the head was swelling each day to the point where it could no longer be sustained; and thought he was so sick that he would die, and this sickness is assembled under the bone above the forehead, between the eye and the bone; and the remedies are such that if the moisture is between the eye and the bone, and the swellings are small, you make a cut on top of the head through which the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the swelling is larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that the corners of the head are open on each side, and the water spurts out when you press it with your hand from inside, and this is not a known condition: then you should make three cuts in the middle of the head, according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after making the incision, take out all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After binding the cracks with cloth and powders, and putting vinegar and oil on it, let it stay like this until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and let the head be wrapped equally, and give food to the patient dry meat of beef or broth as long as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you observe the position of the greatest part of the swelling and the gathering of the water; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes at the back, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the swelling and the gathering of the water are most prominent, and incise according to what you can manage; but be careful not to cut the artery, lest a flood of blood ensue, causing the patient's death from bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
