Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease that is called "catarre" at the eyes or in the groin, and the illness is old, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last treatment so is the cauterizing with those things which will be applied to the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary therefore, when you cover the eyes, that the patient brings his head back; then rub the place with a coarse cloth until the veins appear, then have the patient take off his shirt to the entire cloth; then look where the vein swells, and the places of one and the other are behind the ears, and they are restored; then mark the places with ink, then cut one and the other with a sharp awl of two parts, as far as the bone, and this should be by the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, push the awl under the artery and close it above, cutting also like two strings through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is closed, then the blood will jump out continuously upwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not gape when touched, then you must measure the length of the space from three threads, then sign with an awl and sew up to the bone; and that which is needed for the blood to be put out is six threads, and by chance one thread more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains over the bone point with soap, if pus does not come from apostemes, then close up the wound and bind, and apply ointment as long as it is healed.
de emigrainne	It seems like you've finished the text! The language appears to be Old French, and the text describes a medical procedure for closing an artery after bleeding. If I had to translate the entire passage into modern English, here's what it would look like:
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient emigration comes and acute catarrh occurs, due to the moistors of tears and heat in temples and the old sore is hardened and similar things, and they are medicined by means of treatments with medicine and all this does not benefit them, so we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize it, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patients make themselves bald at their temples and listen to the artery which appears in the temple, for it opens well with its pulsation, and is easily felt than in some men who are too cold; and if it is felt, the patient takes a thread of some cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take the spatula which has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then scrape the thin skin so that you come to the artery, then bring it up with pincers and separate well the membranes that are under each part; and if the artery is fine, then turn it at the point of a needle, then sew up that part according to the length of two threads.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	If she is not cauterized, then all the sinew does not come out altogether.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And remove the blood from the .vj. (two and a half) eyes, down to .iij. (three); and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a double strong thread of silk, so that no impurities come before the wound becomes closed, and comes out in a continuous flow of blood; then cut off the superfluous part that is between the two ties at the same hour, and then, if you see fit, you can cauterize it with the cauterizing knife until the bone, so that the eyes are cut off; and this is the more difficult work, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization is an aid to finish the moles: therefore it is of greater help for the moles.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and cover it well with linen; and when you untie them, be careful with dry remedies that make flesh grow and with bandages until they are healed; and if there is no cork from the artery as much as you work, hasten to close by cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and hold your hand steady so that the bleeding is stopped; and if you do not have this present, put a cloth on the wound so that the bleeding is congealed, and wash the wound with cold water until the bleeding stops, and be careful as it should be; and what is better and lighter in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the wound with this cutting cautery from two parts, but the blade must be well spaced to withstand the heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too dense, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a gap of one finger's breadth, and then when you have marked to join the two ends, and you melt the iron on top so that it reaches the bone, and cauterize the wound in two parts; and let them be far apart between the two edges because it is not sewn with this cautery altogether; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	It seems we've reached a short sentence. "Des larmes" means "of tears" in French, but in this context, it's likely referring to the shedding of blood or tears due to the medical procedure described earlier.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of those who are afflicted flow from their wounds that are on top of the forehead's fleshy part and there is no benefit from any medication done to them, and you see the face of the patient redden, and feel a shaking or trembling sensation in the forehead, and if the eyelids are tense and moist so that the hairs of the eyebrows fall down, and the eyelashes are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this treatment.

de la gresle	frostbite
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers from the eyes things that seem to be frost in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on both sides of the paper; the treatment is such: take heed if the grandine moves from one side and the other, and this is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then peel off each part lightly, then take it with pincers, and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char. des poilz des papieres	the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper that are other than natural and become infested, they harm themselves and bring about various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the paper and moles, to the point where it causes their destruction; and the cure is according to four ways: either by cautery together with fire, or by medicinal liquid in accordance with what is written before or in the chapter on cautery, which is done by incision and suture or by cauterization.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the head of the patient in your bosom, then turn the paper with the hairs towards your left hand; if it has been changed, it is good; if not, insert an awl into every thread above and have it close to the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing from those hairs, and pull out one thread and turn the entire paper back onto a razor; then make in the part underneath the paper, under the infested hairs, all the way across the scarred area, from the large tear down to the small one; then take out one thread and place a small patch of cotton and fabric underneath the paper; then sign above the paper a figure of an onion, such as the bulb of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you see the paper rising which has been divided into two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is need of that which one must wrap in great quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make on the entire space above the II lines you have signed, and begin from the large letter just up to small; and be one of the incisions near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the wick into one of the two corners that belong to it, then scrape off all of it; then assemble the two lips with a seam of a needle on very fine wool thread, and bleed out the blood, and make the superfluity of threads above the II crescents in all things glue-like, if you wish to do this; and if not, have no care, then leave the seam and the threads just up to III or IV days; then cure the wound without a seam of drying and constricting things, for the paper comes back to the solidity of the wound and the assembly of it, but the seam is loose (as said the ancients), and this work is done without fear; and there is another manner: and that you sign the paper with a figure which shall be as the shape of the myrtle leaf, just as we have told, at III wicks cut off according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then consider those who are elevated to small, even powers similarly according to the shape which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you have no power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with which it has a thread, and put it through the figure; and tie one thread near the large wound, and the second thread near the small one, and gather together evenly between your hands the threads; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have marked, as we have said, then gather together the two lips of the wound by suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs on the paper are converted: then you should use what we have said about incising; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The healing of wounds is thus: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two subtle threads as long as the paper and the width of the sponge; and consider the two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of what rises from the oil paper, and strain the two stitches from the two parts together; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that has been strained will die and turn black and become dry, so that it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the wound has some strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, and the hairs can no longer be felt; and this is the form of the two dogs that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	You take a fine needle and insert one thread of soft silk into it; then, you tie the threads together finely and make them as long as a palm; then, order one other thread of fine silk in the case, and attach the end of the thread to the head of the needle; then put the patient's head in your hand; and place it near the sun so that the operation is made clear, for this is a delicate and subtle operation. Then insert the needle into the root of the hair close to its base and pierce the paper quickly as you pull the thread up through the natural hair until you come out at the top of the case with both hairs attached.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the case is pulled and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull the case from below until the thread comes out through the hole at the top and you see it by the vision of the eye. Then pull the case and thread and close the eyelid and leave it closed for two or three days, so that the hair grows in its place and the eyebrow flesh appears; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows with it and raise them together until they are lengthened, then lift them.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness which is called "aleacrati" or the porrittura comes into the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden blow of a wound, or cut, or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of working on it is that you split open that wound, and separate its lips, and put in linen tents, and bind it so that it heals; and it is not necessary for you to use in its cure anything that dries up and constricts.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the sickness will return worse than the first one; but it works with soothing things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or althea and flaxseed cooked together, and ointments made from dissolved diaquilon in some oil, and I enfold a tent, and cure with them.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you give yourself a guard so that it does not close up again in the form that it was before; and those works which we have said are only remedies for this illness, lest it return in the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	This text appears to be a medical recipe or treatment from medieval France, likely written in Old French. The topic is "de la char qui vient en l'oil", which translates to "of the flesh that comes into the eye". The text describes an illness called "aleacrati" or ulceration of the eye, and provides a treatment plan involving cutting open the affected area, applying soothing substances, and taking precautions to prevent the condition from returning.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from a wound and an incision and a cautery and similar things; and the way of doing it in this is that you take a needle in which it has two threads, and you thread them into the flesh, and make it pierce from left arm to right so that the strings come out through both holes of the flesh; then sew the flesh above with all the needle, and the stitches as wide as a splint.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back according to what is needed, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions on either side inside the paper; and be the holes of the two incisions at the two angles of the cut that you have sewn, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure will be as the figure of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the size that its edges are worn under, from what is next to the paper; then join the two severed parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then apply the cure of what we have said about softening medicines, and bandages, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from an incision or a suture or a cauterization, it is necessary that you make a smooth incision below the hairs of the papers, and according to what is written above; then detach between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one should do the work according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters prepare remedies with all their power so that they bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what seems necessary from treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Il semble que vous avez coupé votre phrase...
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs in many people in the same way as the paper above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or do its natural operations, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and the stitches should be so fine that they are not too harsh or too rough, so that the patient cannot tolerate the stitches being too harsh and causing bleeding in the eye; and your incision, from which you will scrape off this assembled thing, should be done lightly, so that the paper regains its natural shape; and the entire assembled thing is cured, and sometimes in the eye there is a salty water and a sweet liquid and vinegar; then put between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and put woolen cloth wetted with egg yolk on top of the eye; and after three days cease from using vinegar and things that are sours until they are healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the corner of the eye is in two manners: it is nervous and resembles a hard, thick skin, and another which is not nervous but resembles white, frozen moisture, that when you touch it with an iron and try to scrape it with tweezers, you cannot; and both appearances begin near the large tear sac, and grows little by little until it covers the entire eye, sight, light, and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	It is known that the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hands, then you open their eyelids. Lift the paper with your hand, then scrape the corner of the eye with tweezers from a small fold, and then take an iron needle, and insert one hair from a horse, or a cow, or a bull, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little bit and stick it into the corner of the eye, and pierce through the entire needle, and tie the corner of the eye with a thread and fasten it above; then scrape off all the hair from the side of the corner of the eye that is next to the tear sac and leave it until you reach the root of the lash with a very fine suture and small forces, and leave the natural tissue of the tear sac so that the incision does not bring the accustomed tears; and sometimes fasten only the corner of the eye with the iron needle and the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the remaining sutures from the smooth part which is the shape.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the suture does not touch the fatty tissue and break it, and that the tear sac is not pierced. And after the incision, pour a little bit of linen juice into the eye, and some litharge ointment, and let it be until the next day; then treat him with whatever is necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the corner of the eye is not nervous and you cannot push in the needle, and the stitches cannot enter, this appearance of the corner of the eye is often cured with medications; and it grows like I have described in the division, and if you see it covering, you will work on the eye of the patient, and take a light, fine thread with a small knot according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift up the corner of the eye subtly, and if you see that it is not decreasing and the reason is pressing, then distill from your mouth into the eye a mixture made of litharge, red ointment, and linen juice, and close the eye until the next day; then start the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no contradiction in the eye, like an apostume (a type of tumor or abscess), then let it drain, and first cure the hot aposteme until it is healed; then continue with the treatment as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the tear sac tissue is harming the eye with great damage, then suspend it with a stitch, and cut out a part of it but not all, so that there may be no flow of tears; then distill in the eye red ointment made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	...et qui se met sur l'œil. (And from the flesh which grows on the eyelid)
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyelids of some men grow red and cover the pupil and stiffen over the papillae and turn towards the outside, and resemble a rosebud; and the work is that the patient puts their head in hot oil, then opens the eyes, and removes all that red flesh with the sharp instruments suitable for it, and supports it with force; then cuts the first layer of flesh, and continues cutting to the razor-sharp edge until the end, and be careful not to scratch the eye during the operation; and make sure the incision is like a spoonful as we have said in the incision of the uvea and in the small forces by which one extracts the iris, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, pour oil of red vinegar or similar corrosive medicines into the eye, and put a cotton pad with egg white on the outside of the eye, so that it may be secure for hot aposteme; and if there remains nothing, and the blood pressure increases, and you doubt hot aposteme, then leave the eye and treat the hot aposteme with soothing things; then return to your work until it is healed, and do the same as a red flesh patch has been stuck in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Mais il est toujours nécessaire d'observer la voie naturelle pour traiter chaque œil faible, et de ne pas recourir à des opérations de force (ovraige de fer) sauf en cas d'accident. Et il ne faut pas mettre ta main dans aucun de ces opérations tant que tu vois que le membre est souffrant du traitement.
des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	They are red veins that appear over the eye, and hinder the work of sight and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for you to first look at whether the eye itself, in which the red vein is, is free from other external diseases than the red vein; then bind it in this manner: command the patient to put his head into your hands, then suspend those veins with all the strings as wisely as possible, and have the strings be fine double cords according to this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two needles, one by degree on either side in one piece according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then treat the eye with force those veins gently, and squeeze out the blood every hour after another, until you see the veins outside of the eye move; and be careful not to prick the eye at the points of the eyelids, and do this work at the hour of noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss what is outside of the veins; and when you have done this, if there is green or red pus remaining in the eye.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to clear everything out of the eye in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it sit for some days until the pains are soothed and you are assured that an abscess is hot, then resume the treatment in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatments:
de la fistule de l’oil	Il semble que nous ayons terminé le texte. "De la fistule de l'oeil" pourrait être un titre ou une introduction à un autre traité médical, mais sans plus de contexte, il est difficile de savoir exactement ce que cela implique.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon's staff call these "arissati" fistules: when you cure them with a cauter and hot medicine as I have previously said, and they are not healed, then it is necessary to cut into the abscess above where it should die, and take out all of the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then raise it to all the instruments of which this is the shape; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron to a length of one head's width, and be sharpened like an awl as it is in the present shape:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your thumbs and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is suppressed, and do this many times, then restore the place with medicinals to dry.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is closed and flesh is growing, and the body of the bowstring is closed and remains thus for XL days, and it does not break out or become an abscess, and no evil happens to it, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other remedy than to lead the fistula back into the navel according to this shape: and is that you uncover from bone the second time by iron and sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered take this force according to this shape, and have the iron spike at three corners, and the handle be thinned all the way up as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the bone near the joint, and move your hand away from his eye I poke, then turn to the full extent of force until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it by the blood that flows out if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows back and hardens the joints, then apply the matter to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the flow from the eye (or wound).
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are entirely opened wide and come out in their entirety, and there is no hindrance to vision or reduction, it is necessary that you instruct the patient; then bathe, then apply poultices or bandages with iron points to draw blood, then place on the eye a compress made of aloe, resin, incense, and sarsaparilla, and then bind the eye with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take cloth sufficiently soft, and double each one in four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need, then bind it over with a firm cord, and repeat the poultices to draw blood without using iron points; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the compress becomes damp, it is necessary that you bind it tightly; then remove the compress after the day and the night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, it is good; if not, then repeat the dressing, cloths, compress, and poultices until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The final line of text can be translated as:
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee. de la bowe de l’oil	Of the back of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but water which is assembled in the eye, resembling an arrow descending, and it is not an arrow; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take his head between your hands from both parts, and move it until you see the water coming up to your eyes; then stop it, and do not let it descend and uncover the light, and look at the patient's things as they are accustomed; and if it does not descend below, know that it is an arrow, and if the descent of the bow string is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient in your hands, then take the subtle spatula and place it on the scarred tissue that protrudes beyond the conjunctive, following its contour with the corneal edge of the eyelid, until the boil is issued; and when it has been released, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek is also good, then treat it with another cure as long as it remains healed.
des aigues de l’oil	From the threads of the eye (i.e., from cataracts)

se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the patient's eyes are now seeing clearly, then the sick person will see before him and the instrument will be in his eye.

de la char sor le neis	It seems like this is just a phrase, possibly indicating the end of a recipe or a chapter, with the translation being:
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At times there are born or appear various kinds of worms that seem like scorpians with many feet; and if there are such, or it has a worm attached by a colored thread, and if it has a soft worm of good color.

And if there remains any thing that cannot be removed, then open it with all the sharp pointed instruments lightly, until nothing remains; and if the abscess or swelling does not burst on its own, or if the suppuration is such as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them so that the pain is stifled and all the flesh is removed, then pour either oil, vinegar, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle works, and moisture comes just to the palate, know that it is cleaned; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a piece of linen thread in there, thick but not very thick, with space between each node, about this much or less; and place the patient's needle thread in their neck at their full strength, and pull it towards a scent so that it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many times do this with children at school, and it is an easy thing for him who wants to do it; then take hold of the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other by the threads that are on the thread.
