de la char sor le neis	It seems like this is just a phrase, possibly indicating the end of a recipe or a chapter, with the translation being:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises in the head of the neck a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large over time, so that it is visible to the eye; and therefore you must cut it out at the beginning, and remove all flesh, then put on it the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays cutting it out until it is large, beware if it has become hard, with foul color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron for it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it once, great mischief comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure touch, not at all with foul color, and you see that one can cut it out entirely, then the patient will be empty and the cut sensible without fear, and cure the place of things constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the abscess is cut out and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of these working cartilages, it brings little profit, or rather harm to some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that you do this when it happens to anyone, if you look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together with a suture, then care for it until it is healed; and if the lips are already split from one part and the other, you must scrape off all the parts of their skin until they heal, then join the two lips together with a suture, hold it tight, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood and frankincense; and put above the powders a piece of a hard plaster or another bonding plaster, and let it cook by itself, then care for it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the suture is that you assemble the solution with either needles or thread, just as we have said in the suturing of the belly wound.
des apostemes des levres	Les apotèmes des lèvres sont une maladie grave qui peut affecter les lèvres et la bouche. D'après le texte médical médiéval, les apotèmes des lèvres pourraient être traités de plusieurs manières, notamment en utilisant des poudres et des huiles pour aider à cicatriser les plaies et à prévenir l'infection.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A multitude of people have ulcers inside their lips that are hard and similar to grains of sesame seeds, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, incise each node, and take it with forceps and cut in each part; then fill the wound afterwards with vinegar that has been boiled, until the blood is stopped; and then apply oil of asclepius, and cure the wound with things that are dry until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there arises on the gums a lump of flesh that the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary to hold it with forceps, and cut at its root, and let the vein or blood run; then put vinegar broth, or other restraining and drying powders, on the wound; and if that flesh returns after incision, and many times occurs, then cut it again and cauterize: if it does not return after cautery; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	At times they are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes they are black and green and worm-eaten, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling; if it is necessary you must have the sick person sit between your hands, and his clothes be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs as they appear, until there is nothing left; and thus do with the blackness and greenish hue, and yellowing and other blemishes, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, then you start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that the teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to how the work shows, because the rasers used to remove teeth from outside the mouth have other forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as possible before pulling it, because this should not be done hastily; for it is a very high substance, and one must have no excuse to pull it. (Note: "raier" here means "to pull out or extract", and "dou raier" means "without an excuse")
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to urinate, it is necessary that you are certain of the manner of the probing.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient's pain departs and he thinks it is due to the good tooth, and makes him urinate again by the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart at all until the bad one is extracted, because we have already seen this in these saints; and when you are well certain of the manner of probing, it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth on every side with a spatula strong enough to protect the gums from all sides; then move it to your hands or fine forceps at the first notch and notch, until they are well loosened, then secure them well; and the patient's hand be in your safe place between your knees, and hold it firm so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcibly, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each side lightly, and move it just as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is pierced and rotten, you should fill it with cloths, in the place where the cavity is; and if you bind it tightly with pincers, be careful not to break it when straining; and you must work very skillfully around the gum for to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return the tooth to the patient with greater pain from the root than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act like the foolish surgeon who, through their haste and boldness, break the tooth and cannot bring about what we have said; but often bring a great illness by the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as often happens to us; and when the tooth is loose, wash the place with vinegar or ash and salt; and if there comes out blood which often occurs, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the extractors, through which one moves the teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have large limbs that do not bend when pulled, and be made of well-made iron, and have teeth to keep them from slipping.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains on the other side, you must place damp cotton or a poultice on the place for one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	Until the place is softened, you must insert the pincers called "algefri", by which the head seems to be the beak of a bird; and they are made inside like a file and this is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, you should uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and insert the instrument that is called "althali", i.e. palanque, through which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through this one, it's good; if not, you help with all the extractors, through which these shapes come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it helps with this instrument that has two handles, through which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other fastenings which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems a pair of great pincers, whose form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is for when it cannot break; and know that many instruments of dens are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise and subtle master finds his own instrument by himself according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancient did not teach a tool for their diversity and I do not break the cartilage or the other bones if it can be helped, so I look for the instruments that are needed, which I have told you, and help from gestures, of what this is the form.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and hold well in order to hold the bone so it does not slip, but rather can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicine suitable for this, and if there is rotting inside the bone, and it is small, so restore all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body and their shape is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth has grown after the tooth and is not in its right place and cannot be filed or smoothed: then file it; and if it is sharp with the tooth, take this instrument which is of this form, and resembles a small beak, and is made of iron with an edge like a saw.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, use this file with a similar shape to this form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth short and short in hand lightly, so that it does not move until it is sharp; then smooth it out completely to no roughness, and if the tooth is too pointed and hurts the tongue, you need to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth decay (lochent) or rot (porriture).
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are loose due to falling or percussion, and the patient cannot press down on what they chew without spitting it out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but this does not work; then you must constrict them with a thread of gold, because the threads of silver become green and rot, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are about to move, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the roots of the loose teeth in place, if there is one or more, until you have brought them into place up to the healthy tooth from the other side; then reapply the covering all the way to the part where you began, and hold your hand subtly and carefully, as much as it does not move; and tie a thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the eyes of the thread and twist them with pincers, and assemble them, and re-twist between the sound teeth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, so restrain it with another thread; if it stays and serves thus all its time, and this is the shape of the roots and the figure of the arrangement of the two sound teeth, and of the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, then place it back in its proper position, fresh and fresh, as we have said; and don't interfere with it unless you are wise and patient, and sometimes make a shape like that of an ivory tooth, and place it in the position where the defect is, and tighten it as we have said, and let it stay and serve like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to remove the thread from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this cord comes from under the tongue or is natural, that it appears thus; or by accident of a wound healing; and the procedures are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your sound, and lift the tongue; then take the nervous cord from wide, as far as the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it's due to a wound healing suddenly, so put the bandage and take out the large one that binds; and beware that the incision is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, then raise the poultice of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place under the tongue a linen cloth; and let the patient clean each night, so that the boil does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If blood discharge comes from it, put verdigris on the place; and if the blood spreads, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then cure with another treatment until they are healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is of foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining to gangrene, and there is moisture, throw in vinegar, and make from a subtle spatula, and free it from one part and the other; and if the blood seeps into your work, put on vitriol plaster so that it is dried, then return to your work until you have extracted all pus; then lift the affected area of linen and cloth, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	swellings of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes a swelling comes down the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pus-like color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it alone until it dies, and then you will cut it out, or it would break apart by itself; and if it is pale in color and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to lance it, but look first if the abscess has cooled down and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his chest be bare, and he open his mouth and take the cautery in his hands, and press the tongue down against all the instrument, which is this shape; and it should be made of subtle silver or fine tin like a small knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue down onto this instrument, and you will see the swelling, then take a needle and push it into the almond, and pull it out through above as far as your finger; and do not touch anything with the cloth, then cut it with the instrument, which is its shape, resembling a forceps. And although the handles are bent and one end meets the other, and are very sharp, and made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, cut it with forceps, which is its shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And they should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other. And when you have cut out one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and cold water, and vinegar, and if there is bleeding from the wound, gargle the patient with water or cooked apple cores or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops. Then cure the patient until they are healed. And sometimes other swellings come up in the throat besides the two almonds, then cut them out in the same way as the two almonds were.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside the throat, that is to say, the small sinuses; and I had very well closed off all the throat so that the woman could not exhale because the conduit was obstructed, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was I had risen so high that it had pushed out two pus-filled ulcers through the two openings of the birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then at once, and I stuck in one of the needles, then the tract ran out, and a great portion of pus came out; then I reset the other part into the other opening of the birth, and I opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I stuck the needle into the abscess, and cut off a part, and only a little blood came out; and thus was obstructed the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut away from this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again and filled up the place that I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I closed it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stayed without growing; and I left those parts, and I was only wondering what God would do with her after me.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the growths come out from under the eyelid and it is inflamed and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is underneath a thick and round one, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the inflamed swelling has been alleviated, and it becomes soft, then you must cut it out; and the one that is rounded and gathered together and is not long; and it is bloody or of dusky colour or black, then you must eschew the incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and its length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we remembered before; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out below, and cut with the II instruments that I said for cutting the II almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover too soon the superfluity which is outside the natural term; for if you cover more than this, it grieveth to the voice, and to the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is sound.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to cover, then you must make use of remedy in the cautery of the sense that causes fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is hot water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient put his head into hot water, and then press the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cautery, and moisten with live vinegar so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and hold the grip of this instrument, from which it is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Je suis désolé, mais il semble que le texte contienne des erreurs ou des incohérences. Je vais essayer de traduire le reste du texte et vous donner une idée générale de son contenu.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more sure than incision or cautery; if it is cured through fumigation in this manner: take calaminth and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and balm and similar herbs, and gather all of them together into one pot, and I put ashes in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and within the pot have one instrument, a spade, according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it may be of silver or lead, and one of the pieces [should be] placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the cord as long as the eye is numb; after it recovers, it often recurs, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess's appearance, for many things happen; and do not do this unless at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put inside the head a quill of egg, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the quill of egg does not let the vapor harm the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	It often helps to insert a needle into the throat or spine of fish, or something else; so it is necessary that you try to see what can be seen, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you see movements in the thing; and if something does not appear and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit when the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of charcoal, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then have it swallowed; and when it comes up, it will be stuck, and you will pull it out; and if it does not come out according to what we said, take an instrument made of lead in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upwards. Be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything go wrong, nor push the bone inside; and it is better if the patient puts the instrument in themselves, so that they know whether the thing is coming out or not. If they put it down, or pull it back up to the instrument with equal force, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is blood medicined by medicine as I have said in the division, through the cure of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, then press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the scab, then remove it with a small incision or with subtle pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hairy cord and insert it into the patient's throat, then place the sharp iron end of the cord there and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the sickness takes hold of the patient every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and move the tongue with their hand often; and as soon as the scab tastes the water, it will break out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not break out as we have said, then subfumigate the patient with asafoetida, at the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will burst forth soon.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot in which there are hot coals, and let it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that perforation is placed the key of the instrument; then pour in your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out but comes just to the nose; and now the sweat will fall, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and make the patient thirsty, and eat bitter and salty things, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	Je suis désolé, mais je n'ai pas compris la dernière partie de votre texte.
