Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses and ulcers, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and it is retained because of these things, preventing the urine from flowing: then boil your water in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, the bladder will be corroded and spoiled; then lift the wound with cold water and ashes and linen, and help the patient in every way you see fit, until he is cured; and it is necessary that all the things you do to cure him, that you tie his two thighs together, and apply medicines to the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small, and it is in the canal of the penis, and fixed inside, and urine cannot come out; then treat this as I say, that you cut it many times, are excused from cutting through it with this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork with three pointed ends.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and wrap it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot go further into the bladder; then push the pointed instrument into the penis gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the point of the instrument back and forth in the stone slowly, as far as you can pierce the stone from the other side; then urine will come out at once; then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it breaks at once, and comes out with the urine, and the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this because something obstructs it, then tie the thread below the stone and the other above, then bend the penis so that the stone is between the two threads, then pull it out, and loosen the thread, and clean the congealed blood which is in the wound; and cure him until he is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the stone is inserted into women and it happens at any time, if it occurs even once, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second reason is that there cannot be found a woman well-skilled who reveals herself to midwives, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a well-instructed woman in this art; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more inward than the stone of the man, because it must be made a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessity requires them to do so, it is necessary that you take a midwife who knows well, and at times one finds such a person, and if one does not find her, then do not bother with any such thing; but rather turn to a wise old woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and command her to do what you command regarding the incision of the stone; and examine very well if the woman is a virgin: then it is necessary to push the string or fundament and search for the stone; and if she finds it, then hold it under the string, and recommend that she put the string on the patient, and grasp and press her left hand over the bladder carefully.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it must be moved gently in stages from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then strike above the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the skin, there where it is most swollen, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move its top above the bone or below, but make a small cut first; then put the probe into the incision, if you sense the stone so close to the wound that the stone can come out freely, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small ones and large ones and rough and smooth ones, long and rounded ones, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	so you may recognize the signs to know its exit.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone stays, put vitriol powder on it and hold an hour until the stone is congealed; then return to your work, as long as the stone comes out, and have tools that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you with your work; and if the stone stays and this is due to the artery being cut, put powder on the spot and strain of tents and bandages, and do not attempt it again, and leave the stone alone and do not remove it, lest the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the swelling has gone down, then go back to your work, so that the stone can come out.
de hernie carnouse	of a flesh hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	It seems like this is a medical description of a type of hernia, specifically "hernie carnosae". Here's a translation:
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this tumour is due to weakness that comes to the testicles, and that material spreads.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And at any time if it comes from percussion on the scrotum, and this moisture has many colors: or it is color declining to yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and so it happens more often; and these are the signs to know this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, I am long like the shape of an egg, and does not open the scrotum, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in the proper fabric, then the abscess is ripe with a part of the yolk, and because of that one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white sac, he feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try to scrape off all the surrounding integuments, in which case its shape will be as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly then what comes after the quadrature, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we heal it with iron, the patient must be purified according to our power and the replenishment of their body; then cover him on his back, on something one pace high, and put much cloth under him; then sit beside him, and instruct the servant to sit at his right, and extend the rod to one of the two corners of the scrotum; then take the sharp instrument, and cut the skin of the scrotum between it in the long part down to the base, and make the cut entirely straight by dividing the skin of the scrotum up to where the sac is white, and carefully peel off the skin according to our power; then pierce the white sac with an awl at a large opening, and draw out all the fluid, and then put in stitches, and close the sac upwards; and do not touch the testicles themselves, but only the scrotum; cut the skin of it on both sides alike, so that if you do not cut well and wisely, the fluid will return; and if the swelling comes forth to your work, be sure to reposition it in its place when you have completed the operation of the sac; then join together the two leaves of the scrotum with a suture, and cure him just like other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	and if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is fitting that you bind the vessels that are suspended, in draining off the pus; then cut off the testicle with everything suspended, and extract the egg, and let it heal just as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the arm is broken into two parts together, know that they are two fragments; then bind the other part so as you made the first equal in length, then strip out the blood, and put moistened wool soaked in rose oil on the wound; and put outside another moistened wool in wine and oil, and put above two swaddles, and put above doubled cloths, and tie it up above with all the bandage that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with torn wool according to this resemblance and sew them together by stitching in the armpit of the breeches, and one end takes up to the fundament just to the back, and the other part to the tip of the elbow; and the other ends on the two angles, and is all assembled in a knot in the buckle of the breeches; and another time has medicine been for this arm fragment by cautery instead of iron cutting, and it is that you take a fine cauterizing tool, and cut the skin of the scapula, and be heated as we have said, so that the white tissue that contains the bone is uncovered; then take the cauterizer according to this form, and pierce through that tissue in small punctures, and scrape it off with a hot fine cauterizer.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cauter should be done in all ways that you can, as much as you can exhaust; and make sure the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and most careful about the evacuation of blood, and beware of the works of cutting; and if nothing makes you contrarily, an abscess forming or bleeding of blood or another thing, then cure what makes you contrarily, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horribleness, then make a perforation, as I tell you, and be that when you are well certain by the signs we have said that the abscess is there, so sit the patient on a high seat; prick the abscess in the part underneath up to the whole spatula wide, and put the perforation deep into the body; and make the hole wide, so that all the water can flow out; then put cotton on the place and bind it, and let the remaining water run out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the water come out of the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a needle or the instrument with which one treats the water from dropsy, of which the form is as before; and enlarge the hole in the wound, and know that the water will return, and be assembled after six months or about, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the swelling of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this chapter there is fear and many dispositions, for which it seems to me that one should not do it; and I will tell you the work and the likenesses of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from the body itself, and even from the groin; and it's in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known by superfluous acidity and ague that is spread to the groin, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess is according to the colour of the body; and it does not find pain, and the abscess is heavy; and perhaps there are heavy and hard abscesses, and of bad colour, and sometimes come from a new artery, or an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by a new artery, it is known by the hot abscess being disposed, when you press it with your fingers; and it does not seem good that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from an inflamed vein is known by the disposition at the expression of the feeling of the fingers; and it can be well done to make a cut over this likeness, and on the other swellings; and thus you must open the fold of the groin, then raise the testicle up high, and cut into the white scrotal sac, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the testicle.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already hardened with these threads, then you must extract the egg and the yolk; and if it is stuck to the syphac or in those things that are inside the vases, then you must deliver all that stuff and the yolk again.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the egg is in its place back there, then you must empty it all out, and draw out the yolk, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once your works are accomplished, then apply the wound with moist wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the swelling of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a bubo enclosed in a wrapping resembling a pustule, with the softening of the parts, and the patient suffers greatly when walking; and the treatment for this disease is equally fearful as the one before it, but nonetheless we will tell you the procedure for it, according to what the old men did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then put the suspender of the parts downwards to your shoulders, up to all the vessels which are near the penis, and tie it tightly, and extend it firmly; then cut with a sharp instrument wide at the place between the vessels, so that they become uncovered, and then scrape off from each part, as we said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples; then insert a needle where there is the double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come out, and tie it again to the other head; then cut in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and extract the corrupt humors; then treat the wound just as the others, where the bowels are injured, so that no vessel may bleed which nourishes one of the testicles; for by this way there is no harm, and if all the vessels bring forth blood, it is necessary to extract the testicles from all the vessels; so that the body does not lose its nourishment because of the cutting of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sphincter anus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this rupture are as follows: by section that comes out the syphac, or stretching on the belly in the part of the bowels, so that the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the sides; and this rupture is either due to a sudden syphac or the extension of it, and these two modes of breaking come from various causes: either from percussion, or jump, or blow, or lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to stretching of the syphac are that there comes a gentle puffing and puffing for a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even until towards the bottom, because the syphac presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is of the incision of the anus, that it brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the swelling has diverse appearances, under the skin near, and it's because of the issue of the intestine and the body from behind the anus.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at any time the intestines come into contact with the spleen, and are retained in that place, and cause great pain to be suffered by the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments for scabies, why does it seem necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is that you instruct the patient to put their hand inside the wound and feel for the intestine if it can be reached; then place a cloth over their shoulder between your hands, and lift up their hips; then straighten the knife above, and cut all the skin from the sides of the groin long-wise; then insert into the incision the needles of the waist according to what you need to open the wound so that the eyes may come out; then scrape out the syphac that is under the skin of the groin until the white hard syphac is uncovered in all parts; then put your index finger on what touches the testicle, between the white hard syphac which is under the skin of the scrotum and between the second syphac, and separate what is behind the testicle and between the second syphac; and move your right hand inside the scrotum, and pull up the white hard syphac to your left hand, and lift up the testicle with all the syphac towards the waist; and instruct the assistant to stretch out the testicle upwards, and untie what is behind it from the tie; and search with both hands if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around the white hard syphac, and if you find anything put it inside the belly under the skin; then take a needle where there are 10 threads and insert it into the back part of the syphac which is after the skin of the scrotum; afterwards the waist, then cut the threads that appear from them until there are 4 threads; then assemble one on top of another in the shape of a cross, and tie the syphac with a strong thread of 2 parts; then wrap up the threads of the stitches, and tie them firmly with 2 parts so that no vessels that nourish them may enter into it, lest an abscess form there; and put back the tie according to the first long thread of it, and after these 2 ties leave the syphac which is under the skin of the scrotum a third part open; and afterwards all the rest in accordance with the roundness that the testicle bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the scrotum until it becomes clean and smooth, as we said before; then apply wet wool oil into the wound, and put on bandages, and also insert the tie which we mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And every time the white sac which we have said is cauterized after the incision, by fear of hemorrhaging of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	It happens often, and let the bandage stay on until it breaks away by itself; and if it delays falling off, then moisten with hot water, and apply what we have said, until it falls away; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this region I have never seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made in such a way as the thread which is together with the needle, in this manner tie the small sacks, after cutting them up lightly underneath; then cut them in half, and treat the abscess of those who are at work, until the small sacks break away; and then cure him as we have said, until he is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes the abscess bursts into an inflammation, as we have said, and opens up the seat; and no part of the intestines should protrude into the groin, and if any do protrude, it is a bad sign, and repair at once; and although if it stays too long in this place, it breeds an ulcer or syphac, until the intestines protrude; and this happens due to the extension of the syphac which is in the abscess, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then becomes softened and swollen, and opens up; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured with an iron in this manner: the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the inflamed abscess from wide to narrow according to the size of three fingers; and then extract the syphac that is under the skin that follows, then take the rod and place it over the apparent part of the syphac; and press firmly into the belly, then sew up the two apparent parts of the syphac on the top of the rod, and sew both together; then extract the top of the rod, and do not cut the syphac nor stretch out the bowel or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the thread of intestines; then cure him with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you sew the boys [hairs], instruct the patient to leave the wound undisturbed until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The pus is constricted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is applied to this place, and it is closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes softened in some men, because the contents that are inside become softened and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to treat it, to have the sick person lie on his back, and tie the soft skin on top of the natural skin; then sew the two lips together with a suture, and if you want, cut off the excess of the soft skin at three or four sutures firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread fall.
dou chastrement	Of the castration (literally "the cutting off")
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore it would please me if I did not speak of it at all in this book; and it is only necessary for two ways: one that the physician knows how to answer questions when asked about a wound and its cure; and the other, because we often have need of castrating certain beasts to help us, such as goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by pulling, we have the beast sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and pliable; then taking hold of them with your hand, until they return to their place and you feel them no more.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The correction of stature: it behoves you to anoint the beast, and squeeze the skin of the testicles in your left hand, then bind the suspensory ligament, and tap on each scrotum with a blunt instrument until they have been thoroughly scraped clean; and do not leave any rough scar tissue or fine scar tissue that is above the vas deferens. And this manner of chastising is more effective than one done by pulling because in pulling some thing from the testicles remains by chance, by which the beast desires lust. Then heal the wound until it is sound.
des hermofrodites	those who are of a mixed sex.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafordie is according to two manners in men: the one manner is that between the two testicles it opens as much as the form of a woman's nature, or has hair, and sometimes in front the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and it has on the palm as much as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of a boil and a carbuncle is such that you cut the congested blood vessels completely, and treat them in the same way as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of their genitals, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of a hernia
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The carbuncle is a congested blood vessel on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to look at; and some women have one as big as a hand, and that is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should mark the superfluity of the carbuncle with your hand or fine needles, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep lest there be a flow of blood, then treat it as any other wound until it is healed; and for another boil that forms on the mouth of the nostril, and you apply to it, and perhaps it bursts forth, and it resembles according to its appearance like an ulcer, and therefore the ancients called it "cow sickness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must clean it, as we have said, with a poultice, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Erraticque seems to be an archaic or obsolete term. After some research, I found that "erraticque" could be related to the concept of "erratica", which refers to a type of skin condition characterized by irregular or uneven lesions on the skin.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is erratic, that is to say the womb of the woman is not perfectly formed, or if the holes are small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident from illness that comes into it; or it is caused by flesh attached, or a subtle or thick growth, and it grows in front, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever it may; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps having flowers, and knowledge of this is through looking at the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the protrusions are close by, they appear on the thighs or the groin.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle growth and it is close to the two leaves, you should hurry and do this: put your two thumbs together, and have the woman sit on her back, spread out her legs; then place the two leaves firmly so that the subtle growth is covered, and the protrusions are hidden; then take linen, moisten it in oil, and apply it to the site, and have the woman stay at home each day, so she cannot get better.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scab is hard and thick, you must strip away the covers like the leaves of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is raw flesh, you suspend it at the navel and strip away the cover; and have blood-stopping medicines such as aloes, dragon's blood, incense, and egg-white in abundance; then apply a wide strip of linen to prevent the wound from closing; and do this for a long time, and then give him a bed of dry linen; and then be cured with other remedies until he is sound.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the thigh comes hard flesh, you must strip it away according to this manner, unless it be infected abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an infected abscess in the thigh should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which do not close normally, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thromboses; and we have already said in the division those similar to them and their signs, and I will say now those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the pimple, when they are deep within the skin, and one cannot feel them, except by means of a cure with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the opening of the skin, which one can feel, are those which one can treat.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then burn the pimple with tweezers, and cauterize it at its roots, then powder over restraining medicines of blood, such as aloes and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the bed for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if bleeding from the wound comes, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and lemon peel and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and myrrh, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he is restrained, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, then make him wear cupping glasses on the back and around the neck without applying heat; then take linen, moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderflower with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is quieted, then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and similar to a sharp headache, so one must cover it as I said for the head; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Il semble que vous avez cité une partie du texte qui traite des "apostèmes" ou abscesses, mais spécifiquement ceux qui se trouvent dans le rectum (la "marris"). Voici ma tentative d'interprétation et de traduction :
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the groin, such as ulcers and scaly abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases which I said in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which comes to the groin, which is not among the abscesses that grow slowly; and if you want to know how to treat iron, look to see if the abscess has a swollen beginning of its coming, and is full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red as you can see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let it stay until the pain is alleviated; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two little stools so that he leans forward, and support him with his back and assemble his feet away from the leg; and be his thighs spread apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then stretch the skin towards the right side, and introduce the instrument by which one works the mouth of the groin, from which this shape comes; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being introduced, you strike the first blow on the surface to know the depth of the groin, so that what enters into the instrument does not come more than as deep as it should, and do not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he put the tip of the instrument above, and that you guide the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one treats it with warm hands, then cover the head, and the spot in front of the scapula; and when the bowels are emptied, then put moist tents in olive oil or green olive oil into the wound; and put the tent far from the wound at the bottom of the marsh, and put on top of the marsh and the elbow a clean moist linen cloth soaked in water or with mallow cooked; then cure after two days of anointing as is necessary until they are healed; and sometimes lift up the marsh and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and Aristolochia longa cooked; then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healed in the marsh, then you must be careful not to cook with iron, but heal it as we have said in the section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first of the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are such that when you see the woman hasten down below, and desire to smell the air: then the child rushes to force its exit; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and the issue is under her head, and the afterbirth with it; and when you see these signs, then it is necessary to press lightly on her belly, so that the child may come quickly; for when it passes over her head, then the afterbirth comes with it, and the woman is rid of its superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes above its feet, and forces its way out through the body or the head or hands, or it comes up over her belly or side, and is converted by chance to the back, and by other bad shapes; then it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how one must aid her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out under its head in natural childbirth, and the woman is experiencing great pain, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, or where women usually do; and raise her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then insert a small spatula made of wood between her teeth like this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and rend the membrane, and cut to its root so that the moisture which is inside comes out; and feel the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, it is necessary to purge the woman with a poultice of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her press and strain with a cloth, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: and now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands come out swollen, it is necessary that you reset them slightly, a little at a time; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on the stool, and lift her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not move in labor; and if the hands still cannot enter and the child dies, cut the hands with a knife which is placed beforehand, and extract the child, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child onto his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto its feet, you should push it up high; and then turn it slowly and slowly, until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them slowly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it starts to jump as far as its thighs, then command it to stop and make it cough on purpose; if it jumps further, then God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not further than as we have said, then turn it little by little, until it be according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easily set right.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't jump as far as we have said, then take muscilage from the elder tree, and oil of sesamum, and melted gum, and grind all into a mortar; and put on the essence of woman inside and above this ointment, then make her sit in a hot bath up to the armpits; and when she is moistened below, then make her take a collar of myrrh, and put it on, and let her stay an hour; then make her sit on the stool, then make her cough and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly touch her belly, for now the child will jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child between her legs.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes into this shape, he put it in his hands gently and gently; then it be placed on its neck, and the legs hang down, and be laid on the bed; and fold his hands gently and gently, and then take the hands to the belly, and remove the pillows underneath, so that it is lowered downwards; and if the infant does not cry, take its legs and move them well, then move the belly upwards, then put your hands in; and rock the child gently and gently; and instruct the woman to take herself as long as the infant comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child who comes out with one hand open, stretching (or: extending).
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try and bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman get up and go; if she cannot walk, make her lie on the bed and lift the legs well; then administer the musilage that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and rock the child according to its natural shape, and make it spit, and instruct her to take herself as long as the infant comes out forward.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child around its neck, and having spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient holds his hand, then turns it slowly and gently; and when it is even, so place upon it the natural ointment of aloes and oil, as we have said, then command that it move slowly and gently; and when you will have done this, so have her sit on the stool, and command that she take hold; and then make her stir.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	from the same manner for all the afterbirth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it happens in this manner to the second child, so grasp the second child by your fingernail, until the moisture is emptied; and if the afterbirth comes up onto her face and onto her neck, so grasp it from the mouth, that it be not retained, and kill the afterbirth; then insert the child inside, as much as it is necessary, and command to the woman that she take hold once: then so stir lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	the issue of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born together, and sometimes they are three or four in a single birth; and this is not an unusual thing, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange things, and they do not live on; I know what you mean by them, that they multiply, and are divided by the spleen which divides them, which is connected to the gut; and at times they issue naturally like a true boil, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue easily, so the treatment is as we have said, and the boil is subtle, and makes them quickly and lightly do what it does; and make thus how it moves towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of more children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	At times they are formed in the month I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of an infant by the measure of their sagacious and glorious size, and it is necessary that the boil knows everything about them, because similar things have happened by chance; so do as it is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	the stillborn child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead or unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to operate by hand; so it is necessary that you know if the woman has good health, and whether she has an accident or fears death; so it is necessary that the woman be seated on her back, and have her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the midwife applies a poultice of 2 parts to her, or she is tied to bed if not treated by delivery of the child; then rub the mouth of the mare with moist oils mixed with marigold and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint your hands with these oils and these preparations; then put them in the mare's leg slightly, then wait for her to give birth or she puts the cords that are suitable to this, and be careful if the child is descending on its head; so tie the cords in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the breast or near the ribs or near the costes, and if the delivery is on feet, then tie the cord or prick it and at the opposite sides; and it is necessary that you apply a poultice to her right hand, and put the cap between your two hands of the left hand, and put it in all your hand lightly, and tie the poultice in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to empty thing; and this is the form of the poultice:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then make an incision in the other direction, or the third if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then stretch it equally from one part to the other, so that it can move out, and let the sutures be set up to hold it, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, then anoint the wound with some of its oil and plug it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if there remains no part, then place this cord or more high up, and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand goes in front of the other, and it cannot be returned by tightening, then you must wrap over the cloth until it comes out all; then bind at the joint of the heel or at the ankle, and thus you must do to the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the shoulder of the child is large and it is strained in the exit, or it has a sharp point assembled, you should push the spatula spiny between your teeth, and make the head and extract the point; or you round it with the instrument which is called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and do the same to the child if he has a natural large shoulder; and then pull out the bones with pincers, and if the shoulder jumps out and strains at the forceps, it should be split open as far as the moist flesh is in the pit of the shoulder; and if it cannot come out, you should cut it into pieces on the muscles that you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, you should make holes until the moistors comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the delivery is easy, and the approach to the mouth of the womb is gentle.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is strained in the belly or in the pit, you should pull it out with the draped envelope over the hand; and make an incision in the belly or the pit, until the moistors that is there comes out; and if the other member are taken away, and the shoulder remains, you should put the needle into the center of the marrow, and pull it through to the mouth of the marrow; then you should put a thread or two, and pull it through; and if the mouth of the marrow is shrunk due to hot abscess that has come, you should not bother, but rather moisten and soften things.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its stomach and you can put it in a straight position, so arrange it as we have said in the living child; and if you cannot do that, then break the spine by pieces, and leave nothing of the sacrum.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the swelling comes as we said in suppurating abscesses that come to the marrow; and if there is discharge of blood coming, so be put in cold water restraining it, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I have seen a woman whose womb contained a stillborn child, and she became pregnant again with another on top of it, and the second fetus killed the first one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she came to have an inflammation in her mouth, and it swelled so much that it burst open, and she began to suffer greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the treatment, and I looked at her for a long time, and I couldn't close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong constricting ointment to it, and out came a bone, and after a few days, another one appeared.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was amazed greatly, because the womb had no bones in it.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a stillborn child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I cut the wound, and in drawing out the bone, so that the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived long in such a way, and soon had a lump of flesh from the place; and I do not recall this chapter until now because, when masters find an unusual thing, they know how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the womb to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the shape of the pressor, with which we read books, and two handles for the two legs of the stool.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the corners should be more subtle than the retractor, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the stick should be 2 palms wide, and the edge of the trees should be 1 palm and a half long; and in between the two bands there should be two adjusters of the same wood, which are fastened on one and the other, half a palm long or a bit more; and these two adjusters are put into the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, made from the wood of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of pincers; and having two handles two inches long, and two thumbs of width; and when you see opening the mouth with the entire instrument, have the woman sit on the bed, her feet elevated and her legs open wide; then insert the two handles together into the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument, as you did with the pincers evenly, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the instrument, until the bail makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all perfected, and their shapes are multiplied; and when the masters have perfected them, it makes the work more rapid, and more elevated among men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	It is not a wonder if you have not perfected the instrument, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second birth is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her breath and then let out slowly, and she tightens her hands to the mouth and the navel; and if she jumps for this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take the root of I poppy, and make a hole or cover in it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calaminth, rue, aniseed, chamomile, sassafras, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked or placed in hot water over the fire; then take a cord or thread from the pot, and put one end in the mouth of the womb, and hold it tightly so that the vapors come inside the womb; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	The afterbirth comes out quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.
