And if she remains after this treatment and is not cured, instruct the woman to wet her left hand in sesame oil or in muskellunge fat from elder tree, and then put it inside her, and make her lie down; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it slowly and straightly, so that the womb does not catch during extraction; but you must move it lightly to the right and left, and then pull.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the uterus is tightly constricted, we have said the cure for hiccups, and fumigation with herbs; and if she does not get relief from all that we have said, be careful that you do not proceed further; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the uterus, that you tie to the navel of the woman, then enema her with tetrafarmaced oil; she will straighten out and recover, and come into a good state; but however, when she does straighten out, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is necessary therefore to perform fumigations that are suitable for this case: none of the ancients have proven the fumigation of parsley and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at retention of the flowers and afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it looks like a similar kind of thing to a cord or a string, and one puts the head of it subtly into nature, and the ends are laid wide on the fire; and the fumigation is done over hot coals, and the scabbing so that it is eaten away, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have the fundament not pierced, but rather it is stopped by a subtle skin membrane: so then at birth, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that skin membrane at its due point, and not with a spear-like instrument, and secure the ligament so it does not touch; then put on linen soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will close again, then put in a plug of cloth or linen, and let it stay for a while, and be removed when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And if this obstruction comes suddenly from a wound or an inflammation, it is necessary to cut it out suddenly, and to treat it as we have said for the cord of linen.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the fundament.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are nodules, and grow larger than those that come from beneath the fundament outwardly, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, it works and brings more moisture, a foul or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas close up again; and are known by this: that they discharge or bring out wind or mucus when the patient makes an emission, and perhaps a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis, and reach as far as the joint of the vulva, and as high as the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula to be perforating to the fundament and not perforating: and it is that you prick your index finger or fundament, and prick a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twistiness.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twistiness, then I prick a fine tent of linen or the hair of a horse as far as you feel the tent or the hair on your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no foul discharge, wind or pus comes forth, just as we have said: know that it does not perforate; if you rush to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is healed up to the bladder or the channel of urine, it lets out urine, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated just to the juncture of the crotch, then the tent comes up just to the place; if there is no twistiness and the discovery of pain around it, then know that it will soon burst forth, and has no cure nor binding by ointment; and in these perforating fistulas there is no strong cure other than surgery, and the foolishness of quacks who interfere with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that case which is not piercing and is not old, by expectation of healing with iron, as I have tried, and the patient lies between your hands on their back; and lift up their legs until they reach above their thighs, and have their thighs inclined towards their belly; then put a tent of lead, or of cloth if there is tortuousness, as long as you know where the tent reaches.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must put your two fingers into it, and if it is pierced by the tent; and be discovered where you feel between your thumb the styphal or the flesh, then know that it is piercing; if you do not trouble with it, then one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	They say that one can heal some, but it is rare; and the aid that one does there, is to heat the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and put it all hot in the fistula, until it comes close to the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those chars are burned, which are like a feather of an bird; and then cure with moist tents made from mud, until those chars come out; then cure with ointment drawing flesh and closing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the arrow penetrates, but does not pierce to the depth of the fundament, which is at the base, and between the skin and the arrow there is a dense covering of fat or flesh, and you see the fistula coming from what follows the covering of pus; then cut off at the beginning of the fistula, and push it forward ahead of the arrow, and apply the cautery afterwards, as far as it reaches to the head of the arrow; and the arrow will be delivered, and will fall out; then pull out the broken skin threads that resemble a bird's feather, and let none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood runs out, and flows between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles two things together: that is to say, the burning of these fat threads, and the drying out of blood and the scorning of moisture; then treat the moistened tents in mud or in boiled meat broth, until the place discharges pus, and the burned flesh falls into the pus; then cure the wound with soothing ointments drawing out tough skin, and they are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes right to the bottom of the foundation and is far from the body, then thrust your thumb into it or the bottom, and investigate it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the boil, and between the two is the cloth or the abscess or tumor, where it is near to bursting, then there are not many ways that give hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three manners: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you lance it just up to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too deep at first, lest you cut the covering that holds the fundament, and there is hemorrhage without will; then cure it, as we have said; by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it since it has been lanced near to the fundament, whether by tent or by another instrument appointed; then cleanse that foul flesh which is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to stay the fistula in the part behind the fundament: if this were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And any time a fistula is made in this manner: then take the tent (possibly a linen patch or dressing) and poke it into the fistula; and it should be on the opposite side from the base, near the skin above.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and you insert one twisted thread into two, and push the tent onto all the thread in the abscess as far as the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced on the edge of the base inside, then draw out the thread from that opening; so as you insert your finger or base; and pull out the top of the thread, and join the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for a day or two; and restrain it once more, until the threads connect the parts between the two, and break through; then heal the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the abscess does not rupture, then make it rupture in all the ways you can think of, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to make a hole in the abscess that is too deep and then dress it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinal thorn or splinter from which the fistula is made is quite sharp on one side and cut-edged; and on the other side it is not, therefore we must not pierce those things that should not be pierced at all, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the membranes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	The tumors are according to two manners: either they are within the fundament, like a piece of resin, and there are small and great ones, and in the fundament there is blood, and there is one or more, and they protrude out from the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those which are outside have little moisture, and within they have a drop of yellow water or a drop of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament is that you command the patient to strain by urine in order to bring out the fundament and see the roots; if it haste, and take hold of it with the tongs, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut off at their roots; and if the tumors cannot be held due to their moistures, take them on a cloth, or on cotton, or on a piece of chamelot; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them off, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until they are healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then enema-bathe the patient with a bitter and sharp enema to wash what is within the fundament, so that it may come out openly; for when the patient takes hold, and the thread is pulled out of the fundament, then the cure is easy; and it is that you take hold of them with your fingernail or with tongs, and cut them off, then cure them as we have said, until they are healed, and so that he fears an incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you bring the stitches according to this manner: take one thread twisted, and insert it into a needle, and then draw the thread up above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, so that it be somewhat wide; and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one part to let the superfluity of blood pass; then place on the bottom a soaked cloth in rose oil or in cerote, and place on the bottom, and instruct the patient that it rest; and then leave it until they cease, and when they will have ceased, so heal them with ointment and other cure, until they be whole.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from the discharge of the abscess or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a discharge of abscess in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you cauterize the tip of a boil or at a toenail the scab above, which does not let it moisten; then heal it until it be solid as it is necessary; and if it cannot become solid, then repeat the cauterization more strongly than before, so that it heals entirely, and be scraped off; then heal it until it be whole.
dou fremit	from the abscess.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance that is found near the body, and goes deep inside; and sometimes it finds the frost, and one senses it as if it were a dead person's tremor, and comes into all of the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a dog's hair from a goose feather, or a strong chicken feather, and put that hair on the swelling, until it surrounds the swelling with circles; then turn your hand around the whole hair until you cover the whole swelling, and push it deep inside, and draw out the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then do as with a thread of silver or iron in this form, and be thin underneath and drawn above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that you can hold it with your fingers, and press it. And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as is said in the book of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make an enema of silver or gold, or melted silver, and sometimes they make these little and big instruments, according to the manner in which they are introduced.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore those that are introduced in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large enema is above wide or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a constriction or the belly is bound, as you see, and the head is pierced from inside; and it has two holes on one side and one on the other; and the belly is either stuffed with medicines in an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there are two inches of space between each hole, then insert a strong thread made of twisted hemp yarn into these holes, and join the belly together as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it up at the front with a strong thread, then clamp it; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or lard from eggs, or something similar, then put it in lightly; then the ministers will grasp it together with both hands until it is quite full, then remove the blister, and lift the patient's legs to the table, and if the medicine wants to come out, so let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night through, that is more great help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse with an enema for the disease of bowel obstruction, and the medicine rushes out quickly, then repeat it until they are healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or abscess, then the blister should be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle blister on which the skin is strained.
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the section on the treatment of wounds that we would now say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they are made, and in accordance with the place or location where the wound is made, and by what means they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by stumbling on a stone, and cuts from a sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from hitting with stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hot abscess: if so make it suture immediately with cephalic sutures themselves if there's blood pouring out of the wound, and the stitching be on the contrary side of the damaged part; and send the patient to drink wine and eat thick foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not want to heal, if the patient's food is thinned out, and does not drink wine or eat meat; and put on top of the wound if hot abscess comes, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in stiptic vinegar; and if there is no hot abscess, if he puts on top of the wound, since it is fresh with all its blood and has not been moved by air or powder that I will say about later; and if the ulcer has moved it, if he puts some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	and if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips of the wound cannot be closed by themselves, then close them with sutures, just as I will say for belly wounds, with stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be exposed of the bone, and swollen, and holds only by a thread, then close it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as roasted testicles and cooked bread, also chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a gangrene on the skin and it does not reach to the bone, then close the gangrene entirely, and throw away pus; then cure it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it torn, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and it is that you put in this powder which heals even when the air has altered it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is such: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and quicksilver three parts, and finely powder it, and apply the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unloosened, if it does not swell; for you do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes you do this with quicksilver alone, when you don't have frankincense or dragon's blood, but the air has already altered the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has moved the wound, just as it was, do not put on this powder; but apply some digested ointments, or balls made of barley flour cooked with water and honey, until they are expelled; then cure him with other treatments until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle forceps; and I will tell you more about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there should be no difference between it and one on the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is numbness, then there should be no other treatment than to leave the cure alone and not put any constricting thing on it, because it hurts the numbs and causes them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the numbs is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if you are skilled in medicine, such as washing vinegar in sweet water, and mixing it with rose oil, and washing chamomile in sweet water, and other powders from mines in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and tie with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and high and full of pus, then pierce or below their place; and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes forth, then stop it, and bind, and cauterize as needed; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the channel is kept, by which the flesh goes, then sew the wound on the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat but set it according to its natural shape; and then strain it properly, and leave it for some time, then cure with ointments of unguents until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then search for it; and if there are pieces of bone, then clean them completely as you can, and what you cannot have, then leave so that the wound festers, and dries up, and closes its issue; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle powder on it as I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and a fistula, then treat it in the manner that I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then see if there are signs of inflammation around the wound where the patient is sweating: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep and all its blood still flows fresh, don't put powder on it at first hour nor bind it to stop the blood from flowing further in depth and returning to the heart and killing the patient; but put an attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton on the wound to suck out moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound three days, or four, or more; so there won't come spasms, nor bad trembling of the heart straining from inside; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Then treat the sores and other treatments, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is a cut from sword or knife, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat the part in front; if it is large, stitch; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has penetrated the bone and has splintered pieces, close the wound, and remove the foreign bodies if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound become gangrenous, so that it will facilitate the extraction; and of other wounds in other members it is a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of intestinal rupture.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium-sized and small; a large wound sometimes causes any part of the intestines to protrude, or the lining of the intestines, by which their insertion becomes obstructed; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than a small wound that a large one, therefore on returns more often the intestines in, if they are not put back warm in warm, because the intestines swell at once when they feel the cold, so return more easily, and for this reason it is better to sew up the middle-sized wound, because of this I sew up the intestine to its place than with other two And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four manners: the two common stitches occur in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds; and notwithstanding they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no part of the intestines has come out, and a slight thing needs to be done, it can be done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him up in this manner: moisten a sponge or a piece of cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook in lukewarm water with cypress and spike, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and at no time does this restrain, and it will be moved that they are alone to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, if you moisten the intestine with hot water or boil and scrape it, because by that means the entry is cleared of something; and if it cannot enter, then make a hole in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to be careful not to cut, for we should not cut without great necessity being there; and this is the instrument to cut it: cut inside into the curve and outside no, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines have jumped out, then put them back in place according to their natural form in their proper location, if you are able to do so, for this is a move.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large and it is in the part below the belly, you should have the patient lie on their back and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly so that the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, arrange things so that the part injured is higher than the other; and thus you should take note of what I say about great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wounds are small, put what you have handy before you, then take a surgeon's needle that reaches all around the rupture and bring together the lips; and this is the common method of stitching, which is to take one or more needles, according to the size of the wound, then leave about an inch at the head of the wound and insert a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make them pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the siphac to stitch; then strain on a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound properly, and then leave about an inch, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you made the first needle, and do not cease doing this with needles until the whole wound is restrained; and the needles should be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles pierce all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot well enter: therefore they should be moderate; and it does not need to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then clip the ends of the needles so as not to prick the patient at night, and put tents or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them from moving, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for it suffices with one needle or two; the second suture is common, and is that you bring together the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the siphac to stitch on one needle where there is strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these holes all four together, then take out the needle at the part where you began, in the manner in which we sew clothes; and leave a space between each stitch the size of a lesser thumb; this suture is known among men, and I sewed up a wound that one man had on his belly, who was injured by a knife, and the wound was over a hand's breadth large, and so were the intestines two hands' breadths long, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I restored the intestine to its place twenty-four hours after it had been displaced, and the wound was sewn up tightly for fifteen days, and I healed it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found or any medicine; and I placed fresh cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it through from outside to inside up to the point where it is inside; when it has pierced straight through, have the thread or sewing cord that you have passed the needle through come out on the other side from inside to outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew just as a tailor sews pelts, and that you leave one end of the thread on one side and pick it up on the other until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks call properly, is as follows: Some people put together the two parts naturally and join one end of the silk thread to the other end in this way: they take a needle or point of thread nearby and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part just up to the inner part at the two ends of the silk; then make one and the other pierce from the outer part just up to the inner part at two other holes in the thread that are on the other side; and this is the more correct manner of stitching and most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this word and any testify to it, that the belly should be stitched with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must put one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when a rupture is between the belly, then the stitching is more grievous than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and the flesh has changed, then put back again the intestine and the skin; then put on the powdering earth, and if the flesh has changed, then put on some present ointment so that the wound closes; and cut the thread, and sew up the skin and the flesh; then cure the wound as with others until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, then put on immediately when it begins to close cotton old, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need another medicine in most simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound may make a community with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten fine wool in tempered hot oil or in rose oil and place it around the joints and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or irritation in the belly, and this happens many times, then cleanse him with black vinegar clisters, and similarly if the irritation comes close to the intestine; and perforate within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more likely to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and this is because of the plantness of their veins that are in them, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the approaching of its nature to the fluids.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tendon jumps out of the wound, so put it back again just like the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you must tie the place that is black, so that no bleeding comes from there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and hang the two ends down on each side of the wound as far as possible to lighten the extraction when the tendon falls out, and the wound will heal.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, one can restore it in some men, because I have seen a man wounded by a lance in the abdomen; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and had become inflamed and became an abscess, and from there came out pus and gases; I put treatment according to what I knew, and did not stop making poultices until he was healed, and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the patient would have an illness in his belly; and there was no illness, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take linen threads to large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the linen thread has opened up the mouth, put it on top of the two lips, so that it holds its mouth shut; and then cut off the head, and it stays like that as long as he can't untie it, then put another strip of linen in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	That intestine stitch causes no harm to the patient and can be tied with a thin thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal in this manner: take the head of this thread from the intestine which has been thoroughly cleaned, and then tie it to the head of this thread with another fine linen thread twisted together, then put the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and tighten it again in the original condition; and as for the stitches of this kind of thread, they are no less than those of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the lower intestines, there is no remedy or cure except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is universally called a "fistula", and also when it suppurates and runs with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the true and hard whitish nodule that lacks pain, and it is also suppurating like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it runs clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times plentiful; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound that does not heal and has no flesh, it is solely due to one of the nine causes: that is to say, by the weakness of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and on top of the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is putrid, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow in digestion, and late in healing, and follows its nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is advisable that I tell you the treatment for fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Abdominal fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestines, or to the kidneys, or to some of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus it occurs in a place of primary member ownership, and similar locations.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come just to the place that I said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it known, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, then probe it; and if the fistula is twisted, then search for a subtle tent of cloth, because cloth folds more easily around the twist; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well probe it with tents, then clean it out through one of the openings, because moisture flows quickly from one opening to another, and purify it; then lance it with all your power that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and see if it is deep in place, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when pressing your hand on it, and the place where he feels it; and once you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a jointure, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places that I told you, then probe it according to what I told you, and remove the falsehood and corrupted flesh that are within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deep in place properly, then you must probe deeper, as long as you can, then put damp tents of medicinal juice inside, and fill them up just to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put ointments into fresh flesh so it becomes healthy again; and if it is not healed by these means, then cauterize it as we said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then probe it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve is not injured or affected, mainly in the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, so let the surgeon remove as much of the corrupt substance as possible until it is completely gone, then cure with things that bring fresh flesh until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and return to their former state, know that you have not gone deep enough: since you uncovered and explored only so far, and removed all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if this is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep to be treated; that you cannot intervene there; unless it is to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can extract it with forceps, then extract it with an instrument suitable for such things, and if there are many bones, extract all of them, do not leave one behind; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut through the flesh and cartilage, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something irritating to putrefaction, and let it be so long as the flesh is putrid around the bones, and then they will have more easily moved the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, restore only the corruption until the blackness is completely gone, then heal the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupted, and comes just to the edge of the bone; you must scrape and clean all up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is closed; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was the young man around thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so much so that the materials came to the leg and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no way to open it from outside. But the doctors through their foolishness worked on it so much on top of the abscess that opened and they let out a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there came a lot of small holes that all gave forth pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors had put treatment around two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to it, and saw his leg and the medicines by which they were treating him, and what was running through the little holes was a large amount of matter; and the young man's body became red and had yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent on one of these wounds, and then searched all the wounds, and found that one was facing another from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and cut into one of the wounds as far as I could see a part of the bone, and it was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption reached right to the bone inside; I cleaned out what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought that there would be no other corruption except for what I had removed; and I began to treat the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I re-treated, and uncovered the bone just as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I cleaned it out, and then I removed it, and leaned over to mend the place; but I could not until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and freed it completely from its mooring, then I treated it with medicines again; and it was healed and mended quickly, and there was no need to re-treat it except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because of the evacuation of blood it would often become inflamed, but it was entirely healed, and in place of the bone there grew hard flesh, and it was well disposed and did not have any harm or evil at all, neither to come nor to go.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated thus: take a linen strip, and bind it to the top of the bone that shows, and command someone to stretch it upwards; and put another linen strip larger than the first strip, and tie it over the flesh above the bone, and hold the top so that you pull out the corrupted flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see that it is good, lest the dressing wound the flesh; and put a hot iron or a wooden spatula beneath the bone to sear the corrupted flesh; and it should be treated until one can see and feel the corruption, and treat it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all of the flesh; then put a tison (tinder?) underneath, and then draw out the corruption from one end to the other with it being as long as the corruption itself, just like we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut into the corrupted joint, and clean out the bone or where the other part contains it; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there's no other device than to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand, or in the wrist of the foot, that thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must ask about this corrosion, how it opens up; and clean out all the ways you can, but do not let the vein or nerve be against you; and know that the incisor and the tweezers for cutting into these bones are many, according to the size of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each resemblance of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so think about the instrument which you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulders may be discolored either from within or from without; and when you have medicated that discoloration with the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, then you must cover that member up to the place where the discoloration comes, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or from the greater malice, which is the defect of the member; and the signs are such that the members become black, as if they had been burned by fire, and after the blackness there follows a swelling of those discolorations in member to member, and takes all over the body; so hurry to cover it up, and if it is from the bite of venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar ones, and if the discoloration is at the head of the neck, you must cut [it], and do not give him space to come to the hand.
