Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cut it at the joint, so that the discoloration does not come up to the arm; and if it comes on the arm, then cut it at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and do thus also when the discoloration comes on the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, then cut the whole foot; and if it goes up into the leg, then cut at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die from death; and the manner of cutting or sewing the member is such that you tie it above and below, and extend one servant of the bandage down, and another servant up, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two bands by a space one finger wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then cut or sew, and put on a linen cloth from each side, so that the sewing does not touch the sound place, and another lesion and swelling will come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If bleeding occurs during the procedure, cauterize the area immediately, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed; then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to my uncle: he had a burn that looked like ash from fire, and that corrosion first came to his toe between the toes; so much so that it consumed the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed; but long afterwards the corrosion returned to the hand between the fingers, and he came to me, and I put on him things that would rebound after cleansing of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he wished that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to do so, because I had hope of rebounding the material; and also I doubted that if I am cutting off his hand, that he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became despondent altogether, and returned to his land, and hastened to cut off his hand, and was healed; and I have told this story only because it serves as a warning, so that others do not make the same mistake if they need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess forms in the fatty part of the body, and it stays so long that it makes a large gathering of pus; and then it suppurates and breaks open, and the pus flows out, leaving the place empty, just like a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as fine silk, and they do not run as far as to the bone or as far as the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and it is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes all the way up to the bone inside, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is so delicate, just like fine silk; and one must cut around that skin entirely, and especially when it is delicate, just like a silk cloth; and it should not be touched because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is putrid and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with fat, then cure it with a poultice thus: see if the breast is large and the abscess that comes out is of foul odor, then make an Egyptian medicine poultice thus: take asafoetida, oil, and larder, equally, and put the mixture in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and apply the poultice to the breast and bind the opening; and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then squeeze it out; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and the pus is removed; sometimes a poultice of ash water is made when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water over them, then let them settle, and apply the poultice, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then cure with a poultice of water and honey, or one that has a bit of larder mixed in; or make a poultice with honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the pus putrid; and when you have done this, and you have faith that the breast is well cleansed, then apply a poultice from which char comes out on it, and it is that you take diaphanite plaster, and mix it with rosate oil and wine; or cure with some medicines and ointments, of whose properties I have spoken in treating ointments; and if the breast abscess opening is small, and the canula of the poultice cannot enter, then enlarge it with a small iron rod, and apply an Egyptian liniment, or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and leave only the place where the poultice can enter, and if the abscess opening that comes out is on top, then cut or lower the place where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowstring is fully relaxed, do not let it loosen hair; and if you cannot cover the breast so as to see it, prepare in such a manner that the bowstring runs down to its lowest point, for when the bowstring is fully relaxed, do not let it loosen hair; and if you cannot cover the breast so as to see it, prepare in this way: that the bowstring goes down lightly and does not leave anything from the bowstring; and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast, and be above the linen cloth that covers all the breast; then cut at the strongest point the nipple of the breast is larger than before, then apply ointment soft on another cloth according to the size of the incision, and put it on the incision of the breast to ease the bowstring, and do not remove the large cloth outside which after many days once; and that which is on the incision of the breast, take off often so as to remove the bowstring, and know what comes from the bowstring, if it is venom or pus or a little or digested or indigested; and be aware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in this manner and you see the nature that runs on the incision of the breast, then know that the breasts have been cured already, and approach health; and then release the bond morning or third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast discharges undigested pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut through after a long time, do not lose hope of health, for the patients approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose intestines take a long time to heal in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested bile jumps out of the chest after many days, know that the lungs are not well; and if the lungs take a long time to heal and are obstructed, mix dry substances with moist medicines, as defined ointment, for it has a great part of vinegar, and this is the final medicine; take defined ointment and make it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine in substance; then cook it and use it; and do the same thing with thickened cooked honey, when defined ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and crush them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; then bind it to a cloth and place it on the chest, and sometimes administer long Aristolochia, and the roots of celestial lily, which are also like flour of vetches and centaury; and use simples or composites: crush them and make powder, and put over the honey that I said, and use; and if the treatment is prolonged, and is not cured by this treatment, know that corruption has penetrated to the bone, or to the hard members, or to the ligaments; then use the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the armpit.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Painful swelling is a tumor that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand, or of the foot, or it may arise in other places; and when it has grown old and one does not take care of it, then the painful swelling comes to a head and bursts and spouts forth pus as long as it runs along the root of the nail, and perhaps all the way through; and there comes an ulceration right up to the bone, until it brings great stinking pain, and the joints of the finger are wide apart, and the color is foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut off completely all the remaining part of the nail, then cautery the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great aid if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy; but if the nail presses into the flesh, starts to prick and wound it, then it is necessary that you put a hot iron under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it upwards, and carefully and lightly cut off that flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on the remaining flesh to remove all of it; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the ulcer is in the bone, then cut it and make it clean, for as long as the bone is corrupted within it, so cannot heal; and if you see the eye corroding, then cut it out of its root just like it has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is inflamed, and swollen, and it causes great pain, then you must first cleanse it; then cut into the angle of the spatulum with a slanting cut above, and be sure that the cut does not reach as far as the flesh which is under the angle, for the patient would feel too great a pain; and if it happens, then place something on top which calms.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a boil on the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The birth of the eye that occurs in some men by chance is entirely fleshy, and by chance it has a space where there are bones, and sometimes it has an angle, and sometimes they are born in the root of the joint, or the birth is in one of the joints of the eyes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any deformity of the elbow does not move, and he who is born with the joint of the elbow, by chance moves; the size of him who is chubby is light, in this manner: measure it from his root by a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that are born in the root of the joint are heavy to heal: take hold of cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or grows to the rear joint, it is necessary that you cut around the flesh just to the bone, then cut the bone by a thread suitable for those things, then dress it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the marrow together come by birth, or by the closing of a wound, or by being burned with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam, so that it can be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so they do not sew together; or put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is sewn, as it should.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a swelling comes to any of his marrow with the palm, cut off that swelling as is necessary.
des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swollen veins are large inflated full of superfluities melancholy which come to many members of the body; and there is more in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer to them sometimes purging with coal, and then anointing with the balm of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron (cautery) is in two manners: one that you scrape and clean out the black blood; and the other manner that you tie the vein and clean it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting (of the vein) is in this manner: first raise the leg with a very hot iron sharp as a knife, until the thick blood is thinned out; then bind the patient's leg from above the knee up to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place or two or three, with a wide cut; then lift and clean out the black blood at your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can bear; and then bind it, and instruct him to eat food causing dark colored stools; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, and be harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of an inflammation is in this manner: tie up the patient's leg if there are many hairs, then put it in a bath, and lift the leg with hot water as long as it becomes red, and swells the veins; and if you do not have a tub, heat it over the fire, and then apply the blistering iron to the spot of the vein near the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then wet the skin on one side, and scrape off the blister from each side until it becomes visible when felt; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then insert the rod underneath as long as it is lifted from the skin, and then lift it to one corner lightly, then apply it in another place on top of three fingers; then scrape off the skin over the blister until it becomes visible, then lift it up as you have done, and lift it to another corner as you have done first; then apply a new blister, or more if you need them, then lift it, and apply it to the back of the heel, then pull out and lift just to the second blister; then pull it from blister to blister until it is completely freed, then apply it; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, insert a needle into all the thread very tightly doubled, and tie it up and pull it out, and insert underneath the rod, and turn your hand from one side and the other until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break off, for if it breaks off, it cannot be drawn out or lifted, and it will cause harm to the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, put some moist wool in vinegar and rose oil on top of the place of the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should cut it slantwise, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one covers the vein is curved, and does not cut into it, lest one cuts the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, one would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civilian vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the thighs, in the warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in the earth where there is not much moisture; and it may occur elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes below the skin, just as snakes and worms come within the body, lodged between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this swelling are such that it comes to the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the swelling begins to come out, just like a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling opens, you must wrap it around a piece of linen cloth that is one and a half to two hands in length, and the node, and let the linen stay on the leg; and every time it bursts forth from its base, wrap it around the linen, and the node; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap up the remaining part, and do not cut it at its root, until it comes out completely; because if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about an abscess or putrefaction in that place, and a bad disease; for this reason it is necessary to treat it little by little up to the head, and leave nothing behind in the body; and sometimes this swelling when it is treated is as long as five palms, or ten, and once a man came to me whose came out of his leg was ten palms long, and when you cut it, it bursts into a boil or a carbuncle, and it becomes hollow, so that all the material inside comes out, and I anointed the place with medicines against putrefaction for some days, then it healed just like the abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at no time should this wound be washed with many waters, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or the foot itself, where there is a lot of pus, and from which it flows with rain; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "bovine sickness", because it often happens to oxen, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body rising and descending, and it hurts so much from limb to limb, until it breaks through the skin where it goes and bursts forth; and it is corrupted by the impurity of some humors, such as worms and serpents and ulcers and tapeworms in the belly; and one doubts its wickedness, because when it goes throughout the body and rises to the head, and reaches the eye, it may enter and destroy the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, one can only wait until it goes: then you must bind the place above and below with a strong but tightly wound bandage. Then strike up and extract it forcibly; and if the arrow is deep in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire on top, so that it suppurates; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards or near the eye, then tightly bind a cloth underneath it. Then strike up and extract it; and the patient must be treated with cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for bad humors and avoiding corrupted foods.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I looked again, and I saw it rise also like a worm to the shoulder, faster than any thing, as living silver when it cuts from place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after ran throughout the body, so that it came to the other arm; then she told me that it would turn again around the body, just like I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease move in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had always thought that pain could move from place to another, but I did not see it in the woman, and I thought it was because the woman's body was dry and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason the swelling appeared constrained; and they did not notice this reason according to this cause in those who are fat, and who have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see that this disease is to be cured, and the patient feels that pain, as we have said, if it opens up so, then tie above and below hastily; and then apply overtop until the swelling constrains back into place; and cauterize at the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure of those who drive out swellings, such as fetid pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The darts (or "saiettes" which refer to a type of intestinal worm or tapeworm) are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they settle.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and broad-tipped; and those with two angles, and those with tails, and those with fragments; and the one which pierces into any member does so in two ways: or a principal member is pierced, such as brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears to you: so you should beware of the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not very deep, then take it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and the syphac vein which is above the brain bursts, is scotoma and swoon and convulsion and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixing up of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and perhaps blood issues from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps speech and voice are lost; and a moist white discharge arises from the wound, resembling pus, and also like putrid flesh; and if you notice this sign, then beware of treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the spear when it wounds or pierces the heart are that it is near to the left nipple, and feels as if it was stuck in something hard, not empty; and perchance the spear moves as much as the hair does, and there is black blood flowing, and chills and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that the person will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a snake bite that never leaves a puncture is when without foam bubbles it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and he breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the snake bite falls into the depth of the abdomen, then it is near the small ribs; and spews a great amount of pus and great pain and sighs; and the patient moves all the members from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the snake bite falls into the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the snake bite falls into the belly, and no thread of flesh jumps out through the intestines, then there is no hope for the cure, nor for the extraction of the snake.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the snake bite falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels a great pain; understand that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and fingers and palms and calves and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the snake is in a nerve or an artery, and it's not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrow struck in the lower part of the eye near the root of the nose; I tried it, and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and he was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow that was stuck in the fat of one eye under the paper-thin membrane above it, and the arrowhead had re-entered, and all you could grab was the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was very large from a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron without handles; the youth was cured, and no bad event came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arabic arrow to the ears: I pulled out the barbs, and pulled out carefully until I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew an arrow out of a man who had it stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die; and then when he had passed 30 days, his condition did not change; I cut on the arrow and extracted it, and it came out without any bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man to whom an arrow has fallen on the back, and the wound above is sewn up; and the arrow stays inside him, and does not change his natural disposition, nor finds harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound above was sewn up; and he thus remained without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And bring a dart to the home of the prince king, which was stuck in his neck, and was one part declining towards the right side; and was the dart completely swollen I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for 3 days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a fine probe and didn't feel anything there; and he felt pain and hurt under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the dart I put on him a drawing and digestive poultice, in order that the area not swell; and the location of the dart appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on him the poultice many days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time, until he felt the dart one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I place a medicinal ointment made with corrosive substances on the wound for several days, until it was fully open, and I tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which had become detached at the site; then I inserted into the opening of the wound that same medicinal ointment, so that the head of the arrow became visible to me; and it healed well within four months, and then burst out so much that I put in forceps on both sides, and it could not come out; thus I did not cease from subtlety and cleverness with various instruments, until I got it one day with fine forceps, according to the shape of what will be shown at the end of this chapter, as much as I pulled it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judge that the nasal septum cannot be restored: I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on what I am not saying; for books cannot take in everything; but wise masters gather knowledge about small things, and about those present and defective, find new work, and a new instrument, for the removal of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come out of the limbs or where they are stuck in but two ways: either by going into the place where they entered, or from another side; and those which jump out on the side where they entered, that is an arrow entering a fleshy part, and jumps out some time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, let it be left until the flesh around is rotten and the issue is cleansed; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let it be left for some days, and move it each day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce around with a fine needle, so that the place around becomes enlarged, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes just up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not pull it out, but let it stay as long as it remains even for a few days, because if the arrow comes close to the sac, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself, and does not come close to the sac, and the patient stays for a few days without bad accident, then the trick of pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very deep and cannot come out easily, then administer tarres around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reset in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent. And if you feel it, pull it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the constriction of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then file it until the wound is large; and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has hooks to which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in two parts from where you can manage, and then break or bend the hooks of the arrow so that you can pull it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you would pull it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot extract it at once, then let it stay until the flesh around is rotten, and then extract it, for the extraction will be facilitated.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding is contrary to you, then follow what we have said of the cure in this chapter; and beware of incising a nerve and a vein, and find an ingenuity how you can draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was when the arrow hit him, for that is the greatest help it would be, and if you cannot, so place him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, or it shows any part of itself, or the skin is inflamed there where you see or feel it palpably: cut then above, as far as the pincers can take hold, and then draw it out: if it springs out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, then leave it alone and resume the extraction as far as it will come out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, put in all the shaft; and if the shaft has splintered, and you see that administration of a wedge would help, administer the instrument pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; then push forward, and if the arrow is stuck, put in the instrument with its point entering inside to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, you must cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then heal the wound as it is necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls in the chest or belly or bladder or ribcage, and is close, and you can cut on it, so cut; and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound, as necessary; and heal it until it is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers with which one extracts snakes are similar to the beak of a bird, and see here the shape: (inserts illustration or description of a bird's beak)
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the snake.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to fit onto the tip of the arrow, such as is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for piercing and testing if it is this: (inserts illustration or description of a pair of pointed forceps)
des voinnes dou cors communes	common blood vessels of the body.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins through which we cleanse ourselves there are XXXI, of which XVI are in the head, that is to say: the 2 blood vessels behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the 2 arteries in the apparent temples; and the 2 veins in the inner corners of the eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the crown of the head; and the 2 tendons in the neck; and the 2 veins above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the 2 veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is located on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "femoral", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the clavicle, and it is that one from which one bleeds, which opens manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is under the bend of the left knee, and the second is called "sophene" which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nisse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears so helps ancient cathartics and migraines; and the qualities of the bleeder, as I say to you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a strap until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: then take hold of your thumb and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, sign that it is about to come out; then take the lancet and insert it into the vein right up to the bone, then raise your hand all along the vein downward, and cut and scrape the skin and vein well two times through the flesh, and cause the blood to flow until you see; then bind and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood from the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth to bleed an old person, and one who has suffered from a long-standing disease, and a habituated ophthalmia, and at the root of the tears' sharp pain; and the quality of the blood is such as I say: and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much so that the two veins appear openly; and feels the knot under your thumb, then sign for him to stop; then lift the key on top of the vein up to your index finger, and push the lancet down, and lift the vein up, and cut, as you have done in the other two veins, and do according to the blood's necessity; then release the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then tie it firmly, and let it be until it is healed; and we have spoken of their coagulation and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein on the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in ancient facial diseases and migraines and headaches; and its quality is that the patient twists their neck so tightly that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point above the vein, and press strongly with your hand or something else, and let about two bloodlets flow according to what you see; then unbind the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is sealed and do not work for a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not suitable that the scars are too sharp and the bleeding cuts across, because the bone is close and by chance the scars may break through when they become subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the armpits helps eyes and the itch and headaches and the gout in the eye and facial diseases; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient twists their neck tightly by any means, just as before; then let it bleed, and the bleeding will be like a true vein, somewhat long but not very wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the scar is subtle and by chance breaks through, then let out blood as needed, and then bind it with cotton and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein near the neck is so valuable that it is used for ague and fever, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes the subtle flame long, and puts it between the upper lip and the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not well open up there, and the blood will start flowing now; and do not go too deep into it, and make the bleeding stop according to your need, then bind it a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two great veins is so helpful for the constriction of the arm, and for the beginning of coagulation, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and for corroding sores, and for herpes, and eczema; and the quality of the blood is that the patient tightens his neck under both [veins] as we have said; and let the master be above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein from long a little bit wide, then draw out the blood temperately, or so much as is necessary; then redo the other side in the other vein, then release the bandage, and bind around the veins moderately that the patient does not strangle; and let it be until morning, that the wound may be healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The salt of the veins above the lips helps to draw blood in the mouth, and corrupts the gums, and splits the lips, and brings down the teeth and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of health are to have the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I said; then turn back the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and identify them because they are black, and around them there are small dark streaks: then cut one and the other, and if you don't know them, and you're in doubt, so cut the thicker of each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, because it's the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein under the tongue is helpful after the cephalic vein has been cut, and it's for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of a surgeon are that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks on each side for a black vein: then cut one and the other, and don't go too deep, because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one commonly saines are healed in two manners: or they pierce to a full great mirtin wide, or olive-like subtle as cuttings through, and is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the myrrh twig is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins smooth and full of thick blood that is apparent, and which contain thick blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the olive-like flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more finely pointed, and is for salting the finer veins, where there is fine, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, is helpful to the illnesses that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to lance it carefully, and beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and a flow of blood comes out, then it is necessary to staunch it, as I said; and he must not pierce the flame, but cut so as with "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open noticeably, you must draw it out, and change to another one; or you want a bandage for it, or sew up the opening in the arm: it opens noticeably; and heat the iron needle, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, you must therefore draw out the arm, so that you touch the location until you feel the pulse; then mark the location with ink, and then tie up the arm, and heat the needle in flame; and be careful not to strike the artery when you see the location swollen, for it is an artery: cut it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protruding upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is arterial blood: hurry then, and put your thumb on top for a long time, then remove your thumb if the bleeding stops, which often happens; tie up the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient's limb; and be on guard, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched, and it flows out, and the medicine is not present, then pierce the artery if it appears, for the head of the vein retreats; and stanch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a peel of fig tree, and make it, and take one of the halves and tie well just to the other side; if the bleeding is stopped, that's good; if not, cure it with the powders which stop blood; and the clotting is not grievous in many cases due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The sap of the vine in wine form is very helpful that it stops blood from the top of the head and from the bottom of the body, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the sap needs to be warmed so that it reaches the nerve below, and if it pierces too deeply and hits the nerve, and it swells and the bleeding will be grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must remove the sap from the instrument carefully; and withdraw the nerve as far as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, split it longways.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The wound of the head is soothed, that it draws blood from the head and soothes the eyes; and it is necessary to wash with a burning olive oil or burning myrrh oil, for this is the most safe of all veins, because there are no nerves or arteries below.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Anyway, it is necessary to seek the most gentle position, and do not cause any harm if you fail the first time, and repeat; and perhaps some men's joints become swollen when you attempt for the first time, but they do not hurt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the saltation is according to your thought. (meaning that the success or failure of the procedure depends on the skill and judgment of the person performing it)
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about washing is that washing is not established solely for the purpose of cleansing health, but also to prevent diseases from coming; and the washing must be done in one of the three veins: it is to say, cephalic, facial, or basilic; and one must wash after breakfast in spring, autumn and winter when the signs of repletion become apparent; and one must wash on the first day or third day after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The doctor who attends the sick person has no fixed hour determined, but whenever there is need by day or night, in all hours and at all times; and it does not belong to him to cure children until XIV years, nor a woman bearing fruit that she be more than seven months pregnant.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be salted.
