Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we bind the nose with goose feathers instead of stitches, and wrap them in a cloth that holds the break together, and the patient breathes through it; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, put a poultice of cotton or cerote soaked in rose oil or a little piece of dragon's blood there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come, he applies an ointment from outside with barley flour and incense powder mixed with almond meal of egg white; then puts on light fires and does not bind it at all; and if the break in the bone is small and it is broken into small pieces, he extracts it with tools suitable for this, then sews the gap, and cures with things that congeal flesh, and binding, such as ointments and unguents suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the bone, he heals it with tents, and puts in lint until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems we've moved on to a new topic. "De la routure de la mandibule" is French for "Of the fracture of the jawbone".
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken beneath, and there is no wound on the outside, and the breakage is only inside, so that it curves inward, then one recognizes this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right part, that you place your index finger inside the mouth of the patient; and if the breakage is on the left mandible, then place your index finger from the right hand, and gently push the breakage inward, and secure it with the other hand from outside, and make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone is split into two pieces, it is necessary that you administer extension of 2 parts, so that it will be equalized.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the loosening of the teeth has occurred, or fracture, then tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on the broken jawpiece clay, and on one cloth double; and on the cloth a large well-made key or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jawbone, and bind it above where you can reach, and command the patient to rest, and give them light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day, and then put back in place what has been changed; and apply a poultice on top, with meal powder mixed with egg or flour of hemp, after you have removed the clay; and apply a light linen cloth over it, and if the poultice dries out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed; many times someone is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a swelling or abscess comes, then apply what we have said many times. (This suggests that the treatment for an abscess or swelling would be similar to what was previously described, possibly involving poultices or other topical treatments.)
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and an open wound together, extract the bone fragment that was not removed; take care to remove it with suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it gently according to your need. (This suggests that in some cases, widening the wound may be necessary for proper treatment or cleaning.)
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all of these pieces and none remain, then close the wound, if it is wide, and apply one or more suitable poultices to extract pus, until they are healed.
de la forcele	It looks like we've reached the end of the text! "De la forcele" is likely a Latin phrase that translates to "from strength", but in this context it seems to be an instruction to stop or conclude the treatment, implying that the wound is now healed and no longer requires any further intervention.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	It seems we've picked up again from the previous text.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	When the fracture is without wound, have two attendants, so that one supports the injured limb and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then set the fracture even with your hands, so that it takes the shape as it should, and there be no appearance or bending.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round spear made of cloth or linen, and as thick as your necessity requires; and then stretch and lift the limb, and strain the spear in your hand, so that you set the fracture even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the fracture outwards because it comes in deep, it is necessary that the patient lie often on their bed and put a bolster under the shoulder; and have the attendant push the elbow down as far as the bone of the fracture can be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the fracture to your hands, and if you find that it is disjointed, it is necessary for you to split it open; and draw out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot join together with any support, have it cut on one of the knives that you have; but put this instrument under the fracture to prevent it from getting loose.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It seems a spoon, and is not a cheek, and be as wide as it is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and has two holes, as you see, and one hole is wide, and the other is narrow, as is the wound's shape that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, measure the wound, and if the incision is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes to a boil, then soak it .i. a cloth in olive oil and in oil of rose and in wine, and put on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is with wounds and cuts, is that you put on the bone a plaster made of flour and egg yolk powder, and put light pads on top, and put a spear under the strap, if you need it; then take a very wide band, a palm in width, then put double cloth over the pads and the plaster; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that band so that the ends of the band are hanging down; and put the splint on the break, and turn the band up to the healthy shoulder, and under the diseased one; and loosen the strapping from each part, and when you see that the strap is holding the break well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the stitches become loose, then restrain it; and have the patient sit on his back, and put a small pillow under the healthy shoulder to lift the joint high; thus, the break of the collarbone will be alleviated by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if bad events come to pass, until 20 days; then repeat the plastering, if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it so, until it is restored; and it will be restored in at most 28 days, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	La brisure de l'espaule... C'est le titre du texte que nous avons analysé ! Il s'agit d'un extrait du "Tacuinum Sanitatis", un manuel de médecine en latin écrit au XIIIe siècle, mais qui a connu plusieurs éditions et traductions pendant la période médiévale.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	The shoulder breaks or its place is stretched beyond measure, and one cannot see that it is broken except by touch; if it appears according to the figure of the break, and resets it according to its natural form, in all the ways you can; then put on the place powder of the mill with plenty of egg white, and light bandages, and put a double cloth on top; then put on a wide and subtle strap, a little more than the shoulder, and under the strap are needles in any part of the shoulder, so tie that hair of linen bandages so that the strap is even; and then bind it all with a strong band so tightly that the strap does not move from its place, and look at it every day; and whenever you feel looseness, bind it again, and put it back in place if the strap has gotten out of place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25, And when this number is completed, then unloosen it, and be sure, for it is not bone that sets itself in a lighter way.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes forward and points downward, then make it level by cutting into the flesh above it, and apply ointment to the area as we have said for soothing an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! La phrase "de la brisure du pis" est probablement liée à une blessure ou une fracture du poitrail (la poitrine) d'un animal, peut-être un cheval.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it subsides to the bottom, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks flesh, and swells quickly, and possibly vomits blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and the condition seems grave.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts a cushion between his shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and he gathers the ribs of the two ribcage with his hands, and gently tries to put everything in every way that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put poultices and bandages on the gentle salt or other light wood on top of the broken bone, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it on the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the string around to the back, and tighten it gently, and reward each hour with an oil dressing, and if it swells, then tighten it; and if it is necessary to release it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry and release it, and clean the poultice, and address what has come in ways of cures; then remove the poultice, and tie it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons une traduction d'un texte médical ancien, probablement du moyen âge.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in their large parts behind the back, and at the head within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and this one knows well through examination by touch.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you place it evenly over the break, as it is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and bind it with an iron band, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is sloping inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncture, just like a pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and the person sweats with needle-pricks, and burns and vomits a great quantity of blood, and this is a grave illness, and the ancients have put great ingenuity.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the stomach, so as to push the break outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses form there, if they have not already formed.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to that, let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said among themselves that one applies cupping glasses to the place in order to draw out the bad matter, and this seems to be reasonable; nevertheless, doubt exists that the cupping glass may draw out the superfluities to the place by reason of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said among themselves that the place should be covered with moist wool in hot oil, and one should put tents between the ribs to set the hurt evenly around, then it should be treated as a case of pleurisy, from meat and from medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure due to the bone which pushes against the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then you must cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put something under the instrument to protect the skin; and then you must saw through the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and heal them with poultices until they are sound.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes forth, then apply damp cloths soaked in rose oil on it, and apply the poultice to its place; and cure the spot itself of what is needed for the abscess, and be careful with linen on the surrounding area where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	...of the break of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	At any time, there comes a fracture of the double bone of the neck, and it happens when it bends; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, see if you observe their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they are moved and feel well when one holds and pricks them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient has been cured, if one puts a cure there.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, see if the legs are softened, and if the excrements are in the hands, and there is vomiting and defecation without will; and when one has been cleansed on their belly, if there is defecation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is sitting on his back and wants to sit down, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Be aware that it is mortal: if you do not work in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you bind them if there is an inflamed abscess, and put oil of roses or egg oil on the spine until it is calmed down; then put a comforting and drying plaster on it, and tie it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not let them sleep on that part where they feel pain, as long as they are being healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone has cracked open, it is necessary to cover the wound with a cloth; and remove the bone, then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then heal it with ointment dripping fat meat until it is healed. And if the ligament of the bone is broken, which is called the "ligament of the knee", take your pouch from your left hand and put it equidistant in your right hand at your power, then put the plaster and bandage on it, if you need to; then bind it tightly, and if there are any bones cracked open, do so again, remove them, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	...the fracture of the bone of the hip.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	...It rarely happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a very little decrease in strength at the head; and they make an incision long and decline towards the perpendicularly, and come to the painful place of the patient, and puncture, and swell up what has been broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is this: that you extend your hand above, so much as it reaches over the fracture; and know which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only in the head, place equal to the break, so much as it be of natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is too long, or it descends inside, then make the patient lie on his belly, so much as the restoration of that break appears to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, place on the splint, then put on a wooden or hazel stake, and bind the break, so that it does not move; and lay the joint under the ribs, as much as the equilibrium is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to lie on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swelling comes, do not touch it, as much as the swelling is appeased, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it so as it seems fitting, if there is no bad accident; and that is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the arm.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The arm is what is between the elbow and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then it must be restored according to one of two manners: one of which is that you take one straight stick of meadow juniper, larger, shaped like this:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with two strings, and bend them upwards, and make the patient sit on one seat; then put the broken arm over the stick, so that it comes to rest in the crook, and have a curved piece of wood in the middle; then put something heavy on top or have someone extend it downwards; then place the splint so that the break is equal with his hands together, as much as the break returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is that you bind the patient on his bed, and tie the hand to their neck, then command two ministers that one hold what is above the break with their hands, and the other hold below each string, and extend each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the thread under the bandage, and on the bandage, and stretch each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the bandage is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you put the middle thread under the bone, and the other towards the edge, under the bandage; and similarly if the bandage is on the side, it is necessary to put the lighter thread slightly, without labor, until the bandage is even above the bone, and above the edge; then tie the bandage, as is necessary, and tighten it, if swellings do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if swelling comes, do not bind it again until seven days, and put on a damp linen cloth and rose oil, so that the swelling is calmed; then bind it, and the manner of binding is to put the splint on the break, then bring the arm onto the elbow, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the wrapping, and bind on the elbow and on the arm, so that the arm is in its natural position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not in its proper position, then use splints, and put on the break a larger and stronger splint than the others, with two spaces between each one, and have each splint be so large that it passes over the break three fingers from each side; then bind on the splints, just as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more strongly and less apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, in the place that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, so let it be left to itself until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days at the ligature, lest pruritus or inflammation does not come into place, or the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the discharge, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident comes to it, then do not remove the ligature until after three days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, and put his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken member does not move, or be loosened the ligature; if the discharge comes by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned beforehand, in such a way that the food is at the first subtleties; and when he begins to recover, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset within 40 days of all things; and then one must loosen and administer bath and medicaments of ointments to set the joint in place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and swollen, it should remain loose for 7 days or 2 months.
de la brisure du bras	Il semble que nous ayons terminé le texte sur la manière de traiter une fracture du bras en Moyen Âge. Merci pour la traduction et l'interprétation ! Si vous voulez, on peut poursuivre avec un autre texte ou discuter de ce qui a été dit jusque-là.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Il semble que nous reprenions une description anatomique du bras. Les "fosciles" (ou fémurs) sont les deux os longs du bras, l'un étant plus petit (le petit fémur) et situé près de la poitrine, tandis que l'autre est plus grand (le grand fémur) et se trouve sous le petit fémur. La description mentionne également que parfois, les deux os peuvent se briser en même temps.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light and the recovery; and when the great ones are broken, the recovery is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together in one piece.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then you should have it slightly extend and put in place.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great bone, then you must have it stretched more strongly; and stretch out on the cushion, and pin up the patient's hand higher than the others, and the little ones lower than the others, and let the patient cross himself over him, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch out the assistant's arm to the part under his hand, or to the joint, and another assistant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are pieces in the break, then put each one back in its place, and if any of them is loose so that you can't hold it steady, and you can't restore it to its place, then do an incision and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; take its care. (Note: this seems to be a summary or reference back to another part of the text, rather than a literal instruction)
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the treatment on the sore supervene abscesses, then apply an ointment made from rose oil and white wax, which is not too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth over it subtly, so that the hot abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the ointment, and apply the poultice of the mill powder with a great deal of egg white; then put on the stars, and the star of the fracture should be immediately more firm, and slightly wider than the others; and know that it must have six or seven stars in several arrangements: whether the break is in one bone or two; and keep the break higher up than anywhere else, and always less loosened, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and the cloths above the break should be soft and moist, and not hard nor sharp; and the thread by which it is strained should be linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you bathe the member with hot water until those itchings are soothed; and let the member not tightly rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then recommence the bandaging, and if the ligament is loosened and the bone separated, and a similar thing, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too narrow, then you should soften it with one pot of water, and let it be thus for some days, until the swelling goes away, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not remove the bandage until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or inquire around the joint, then he stretches his hands to his neck, and let his necks be even, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this breakage is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	It seems like you're referring to a specific medical text about treating broken limbs, likely from the medieval period. The text is written in Middle French and appears to be discussing various treatments for different types of fractures, including those of the hand.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and also on both wrists there is a small fracture; and it only causes them to become swollen many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the wrist of the hand is broken or swollen, it should that the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of him also; then place his hand on the stretched cloth, and extend the broken bones, and put them even with the mirror, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there is no swelling, then he places a stake according to the quality of the break; and it should be wrapped in one linen drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the belly of the wrist, he makes a ball of cloth and commands the patient to press it against his broken wrist; and then ties it with a long drapeil, and the splint should be of good wood as large as the hand, and tie it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, it should be that you put a splint above and another one below in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand, and stop the string between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, put it in place as it should be; and tie it with the wrist, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and don't let it move; and if the fracture is on another finger, such as the index or one of the others, put it in place, and tie it with the healthy thumb that is behind it; or tie all together in one bandage, so that it doesn't bother you; or put a splint over it, as I said before; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the hot swelling, and dry out what comes to it.
de la cuixe brisie	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is clearly visible when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists in tying one thread above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his back, then stretches each thread of his ministers to an equal part; and that is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near to the root of the thigh, it should be one of the ligaments towards the armpit, and the other ligaments below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and then it should be one of the ligaments by the knee, and the other extension downwards; then put the splint on the bone with both hands so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the poultice and the bandage, so that the abscess does not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a warm swelling, let it subside then return to your work and your cure; the tying is done in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap over the break with a strong doubled bandage two or three times, and leave the superfluities; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the hip, and push the long thread between the thigh and leg below, and come to the head of the thread above; then turn on the leg and on the thigh the bandage, then put over the break stitches, and put a stitch on the bone of the leg; then wrap up the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to set the stricture equal; then begin to tie firmly three turns or four on the break; and as you go higher on the break, less the stricture; then join the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and the thigh, and tie three stitches above; then go down to the bottom at the head of the thread, so that you come below the foot; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it so; then if there is no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't heal, then loosen the bandage and address what is happening, as we have said many times before. And if there are fragments of bone that are protruding, then it needs to be cleaned, if possible; and if not possible, then it needs to be cut out and pulled out; and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And whenever the thigh is broken, so that one puts pads on it, as in the armpit and on the arm; however, in this treatment made no swelling occurs.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the hollow of the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groin fold there is often a break, but it folds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a slit or an incision, and has to be all stitched up, and without stitching, and that seems good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is thus: one puts back what was out of place on its hinges as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint, and if you need to, put an iron rod round it, and bind it so as it should be; then replace all the settings that we have said for other breaks, such as applying heat and similar remedies; and apply whatever is needed for each accident until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it has a similar breaking as when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns every which way.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone (fibula) is broken, it turns outward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the big bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly; and the limb turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then make an extension and set it straight, and bind the straps equally; but nonetheless, it is necessary if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, that the extension be smaller and lighter; and adjust it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two wooden splints that fit the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to below it. Then wrap them in two layers with a bandage above and below, and tie them together in the middle; and at this point the leg will not be able to move to the right or left, and thus it is well. And some give one strip of wood, long as the leg, and made of wood, and place it on the leg to prevent movement, and properly make up what is lacking in the break where there is an open wound; and every day stir the leg around to see if there is any hot swelling or other accident; and take care of it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of the bones of the foot.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle there does not come a break, but to the two bones of the foot sometimes comes a break and the small toe, and there is no fault that does more harm in other arrangements.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there has been a break in the two bones of the foot and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put such patients on their feet on the earth, just like they would go, and then place your own foot over theirs, at the spot where the bones are raised, then press them so hard that they return to their places; then apply the splint and bind it with cloth, and place under the lower part of the foot a small table, two inches thick, then tighten the splint onto the foot slowly, then once you have wrapped the bandages around and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, then loosen the bandage, for you will find that the bones are aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are some toes broken, then put them back in place, just as we have said to put the toes of the hand back in place. Then place a splint on the broken toe according to its length and be a little wider, then place under the foot that table I mentioned, and tighten it slowly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped up in one cloth of linen, and strain the table under the foot; and so as they should be on top of the end of the table out from under the lower part of the foot, that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget to remember the other things that I have said about other breakings, since we have discussed them; and treat each injury according to its needs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Une autre partie du texte !
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's natural place is broken, then make her sit down and enlarge it; then incline her to the back part and hold her by the back; then fill the woman's natural opening with cotton, and put in as much as the stomach; then throw out the woman and lift up the back little by little, and thus the cotton will jump until it comes into the woman's natural place, and the bone will return with the stomach. And when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this seven days or so: then the breakage will be restored; and if you see, take a bladder of grass and attach a cord to the penis, and insert all the bladder into the natural place; then blow strongly on the cord until the bladder is inflated inside: the natural place will return to the breakage; then fill it with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the shoulder of man or woman is broken, fix it in the same way as we have said for the femur; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and practice into it and understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in many dispositions the right way of restoration: understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap a cloth around it and leave it for three days or near that: and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Je vois que nous avons changé de sujet !
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the person who has a break with a wound, just as great as the bones of the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be cured now, so that the stitches we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals but becomes infected with vitriol, and you don't have anything else, then start restoring the break again at the same hour or on the same day, lest abscesses form and it doesn't come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come out, then leave the restoration just until the ninth day, so that the abscess is quieted, and don't touch it on the third day or on the quarter, for you would bring a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on top of the skin uncovered, it is necessary that you put it in a gentle point to your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not ready for you to put it evenly on your hands, then make the instrument which is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches long, and its width according to the quantity of the wound; and so it is necessary that the craftsman take 3 or 4, according to what he needs in each cure of a break; and let it be rounded and somewhat thick, so that it does not bend at the compression on the member under your work, and be angled forward, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved end must be put on top of the visible bone, and push it in once, so that it returns, and be even with one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone well, you must cut off the top of the bone until the instrument has possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot restore the bone to its place, as we have said, then take a suitable instrument, such as an awl or gouge, and scrape out what remains in the bone of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reduced, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it has been set back into place, then moisten the cloth with black vinegar and dry it properly; and do not put cerote or any other oil on the wound where there may be putrefaction and corruption; then administer ointments when you have set the bone right, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover all around it, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not compressed with the breakage; and many times this has been done by foolish healers, and death or corruption has come upon the patient once or twice; and the splinting is more gentle and softer than other breakings.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that some evil occurrence may happen to it, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, then do not put on ointments; but envelop around it, instead of ointments, strong cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two the bow of the wound becoming swollen, then remove what you have put on top with vinegar and put salving for healing wounds, such as tetrachlorated ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the member two times a day, in the morning and at nightfall, until it is solidified and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be aligned in such a way that the bowels go down slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it passes many days and cannot heal but rather the bowels keep coming out, know that there are small pieces of bone in it, for which reason you should sew up the wound with a thread, and take out all these loose fragments that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the member, such as the shin or shoulder bone, and other similar large members, then do not pull it out, for many times death comes from this, but leave it until it rots; perchance it will fall out after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	bruises that come on top of the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come back many times after the healing of the bruise, especially when it is near the joint, and it's a sad thing to see the figure of the member; and perhaps the member cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care if the swelling is fresh: administer medicinal purges, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, aloe vera, and similar others, in the same way that you would take any of these things or all of them together, and mix them with purgative vinegar or with beaten egg or with oil; and apply them to the wound with a compress, and bind it tightly, and do not loosen it for a day; then loosen it, and start again another one, as long as the swelling is gone; or you strain over a well-made cloth; because the properties of cloth are that they remove all the swellings on the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, then cut off the excess above it, or have it shaved by a barber until it is gone, and cure it once it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and after it remains weak and fragile in the member, it happens for many causes: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or because of excessive bruising; or due to very great movements, not at its own time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and make the body tender, until the blood is multiplied in it; and administer baths to them, and give them joy and cheerfulness; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and often soak with hot water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and restore it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and leads to great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the swelling and torture are fresh, it is necessary to soak them with hot water, or cook soothing herbs, such as valerian leaves, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a soft plaster, such as well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of valerian, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with linseed meal, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes a boil is lanced because of constant and prolonged rubbing with damp hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And stir up movement in the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting has turned into a hardened and calcified state, like stone, and it needs to be cut out with a scalpel, then cover just up to the bone, cutting carefully and lightly with a fine edge; and apply cauterization and a poultice in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of Dislocations (or Fractures)
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	A dislocation is a displacement of some joint from its place, because it cannot move, and the member is badly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation comes to someone, it is necessary to reduce it immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling increases, and by chance puts pressure on the area; therefore it is not necessary to move it until it has swollen: many times bring about spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient sweat, then let him go until the abscess has subsided; then bathe the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member as the treatment comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of Dislocations from the top of the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones (or mandibles)
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Something happens when the jawbones are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both jaws is in two ways: or they are slightly displaced from their place, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the breast, and cut off the saliva from the mouth that it can't hold, nor close its mouth, and enclose its tongue with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in a few dispositions (or without much trouble).
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it quickly, and not delay; and in such a manner that the attendants grasp the patient's head, and insert the mirror's cup into one of their hands in the root of the jaw dislocation within the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside to make equal; and instruct the patient to loosen his jaws and move them all around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the ministrant makes it even, so that it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the reduction is difficult, or even if it's both jawbones together, you should soak them in hot water and oil, until they are softened slightly; nor delay the reduction, as we have said.
