Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment, and the patient's mouth becomes well swollen with softened flesh, then put moist cloths on the face made from rose oil and wax, and then tie it lightly with soft strings; and have the patient sleep on his back, and his head be supported by two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strains himself to chew, but take light food until the pains are removed, and have the jaws been closed; and then loosen what he wants lightly, and do not trouble him to open his mouth while eating and drinking, until the jaw is well closed and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not converted back to their usual state, then fever and severe pain ensue, and perhaps belly cramps, and possibly vomiting of cold, clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a mortal condition; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the elbow (or forelle)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The elbow cannot be dislocated from the side towards the spine in its continuation, and it is always dislocated to the outside, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back often and stretches out his arms; and then presses the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the poultice and bandage, and hold it in place; and the joint which is towards the shoulder cannot dislocate itself; if not, and if it does dislocate once, you should reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the poultice and bandage, and hold it in place, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and likewise bring back the joints of the spine when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the Dislocation of the Shoulder (or Spaulle)
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: of which one is when it dislocates towards the hollow part below; and the second is when it dislocates towards the back part; and by chance it dislocates upwards, and such cases are rare; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; and many times dislocates downwards towards the hollow part, especially in those who have little flesh, for then it leaps out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it leaps out at a distance, and returns at a distance.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they are percussed or crushed, and the shoulder becomes inflamed with a hot swelling, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine it carefully, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation occurs when it falls downwards towards the hollow part, and makes a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and below the hollow part to the toucher the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move in any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the toucher; and this type of dislocation is not to be returned when it is new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministrant lifts the patient's hand up high, then puts their thumbs under the armpit, and lifts the joint with force up to its place; and the ministrant lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it back in; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in three days, the patient must be bathed in hot water; and the attendant should apply a softening and soothing mixture, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and mellilote in water, and it should be applied; then the patient should be placed on their back, and under the shoulder, an equal woolen strap should be placed, not too soft nor too hard, then the physician's staff should be placed at the heel of the patient, and lift the head of the shoulder strongly, and pull the patient's hand; and another attendant should hold the patient's head so that it does not move down; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see it thus: and is that you make a man who is greater than the patient be present; and he should stand straight towards the side, and push the patient's shoulder under his own, and lift the bed up high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant should pull the patient's hand down towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can carry with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation will come back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And reset it in another way: and is that one puts a long stick into the earth, whose head is as sharp as a spit, and not too big or too thin; then it's placed under the patient, but so that he has wrapped himself softly over it, and the patient is leaning on the length of the stick; then his hand will be extended from the other side in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth over the top of the skewer so that the skewer does not hurt the patient, then place it under the armpit of the patient; and extend your arm over the length of the skewer, and tie the elbow on top of the skewer, and the arm at the hand, then place the arm over a wooden splint of one and a half fingers in width, and have the hands extended downwards, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, then you should put under the armpit a linen ball of equal size, then apply an ointment made with flour powder, incense and egg fat, over the entire shoulder and around it; then tighten the bandage under the armpit gently, and turn the cloth over the ointment, and bind the hand to the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat lightly, until the members are comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat again in 5 or 7 days, and move him; and if it is firm and has not softened, it means it is sound.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three punctures, as it is shown before the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this and after 7 days, the joint still does not hold and cannot lift their arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs towards the spine, and shoulders, or back, is caused by a blow, and stretching of the hands, and it administers another type of injury; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness in the member and delay in movement, then have the patient bathe many times until the stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the Dislocation of the Shoulder (or Coute)
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in parts, and returns to its place in parts; and it is dislocated from all sides, and also before and behind, and the dislocation is not easily reduced, because one can see it well and feel it well; and it occurs according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the cut of the patient with the sinew, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reduce it in such a way that hot swellings come, because if hot swellings come, it will be more painful to reduce; and perhaps it cannot be fully reduced at all, especially when it occurs behind; then it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death ensues.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the reduction is such that when it can be reduced, you should extend their hand with your two hands; and their arms should be stretched out, and the ministrant's hands around the shoulder joint, on top of it and underneath, and push the joint into its own place, or to the root of their palm, until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when they bring their hand to their own hand, and firmly press the root of the palm on the shoulder that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and two ministers extend the arm, and tie it with two ministers, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, he oils it with some oil to soften the joint, then place the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on dry poultice with egg white, and bind it firmly, and hold the arm at the neck of the patient, and let it be for a few days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the poultice and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, then have him bathe and rub well, and press so that it is eased; or put a sheep's fat ice on the joint, then let it stay for one day and night, then take it out and put him in the bath; and when he sweats, have him rub the joint temperately, then put the ice back on, and then put him in the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you wish, put moistened linseed paste heated with wax on it, and hold it there; so it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return to place is slighter than that of other joints Nevertheless, it must be put back in place hastily, in the same manner as it was dislocated, even if the place swells or becomes inflamed with a hot aposteme.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reset is that you put the ailing hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand, and have the scribe make them even, so that he puts his palm over the appearance of the joint, and then push it back in as far as it will go. Nevertheless, you must see if it is well in place; then put the patient's palm of their hand on a table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then the patient puts their hand on top of a table, and the physician places their hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's well If not, then the patient is restrained with soothing plasters on the abscesses and left without starting again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after any days, the twisted joint remains; and do not harm anything to the patient until their hand is swollen, and they cannot restrain anything at all: then know that the nerves are crushed or the arteries; for there is no other remedy worse than restraining by a cautery near the case, and perhaps it's worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the ointment that we have mentioned, then bind and leave it for 5 days, then remove the binding and let it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then wet the hand with hot water and rub it gently until it is warmed up.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	the dislocation of the wrist
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the wrist of the hand is dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the stomach; then it swells and you push the dislocation to your pouches until it returns, then hold the head of the wrist and pull it towards the side where it was separated; and let it be for two days, and then make it equal on that day; and from there tie it, as we said, and untie it every day, and move it around, and tie it back; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated in the stomach of the hand, and do so as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the spine (or more specifically, the vertebrae) at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several that are dislocated, then there is no treatment, for death hastens the ailing person.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the evacuations jump forth without will, nor can they hold them, and many times are softened any member, or the two thighs or the two arms or one; and many times is moved the heel to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilletiz": the cure is that you turn back if the gilletiz came from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing of it all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or percussions or similar things, the ancient men said to be manners of cures by great words, where there is not in all a great profit; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the chest in front, there is no remedy nor healing; and also that which comes straightly on both sides, and one cannot cure better than that which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient lies stretched out on their face in an equal place, and has a strap under them so they do not bleed; then stick two skewers at the head into the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie one cord behind the armpits of the patient, and another behind the thighs, and knees, and ankles; and the two servants know the cords, one to the head and the other to the feet, among the two skewers; and be well fastened, the skewer as we have said, and the physician puts their palms on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long, and hollowed out below the surface, and have the patient lie on their side, and place the head of the board beneath the surface, then put the middle part of the board on the spine; and have the mirror held over the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see [something], do it to the turn which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you do that by fixing two torches at the head of the patient, one arm long, and two others towards the feet; and between each torch, there is a space an inch long above and below; and in each torch there is one turn, or where the cord turns, and the torches are firmly fixed to the ground so they do not move; and between the two torches there is one other torch turning, on which the cord turns, and there are two small torches a hand's breadth long, to turn the cord; and then tie the string that is between the upper bones of the neck to the head torch, and the other string towards the feet to the other torch, and each assistant turns their torch so that all the string is turned, and the master makes the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is evened out, so put on desiccative ointment with an abundance of egg, and then bind them up, and then the iron band of a tablet three ells long, which stretches out the place of the elbow and the part of the spine that is healthy, then tie it tight with a cord, just as we have said, and use gentle poultices on the patient until they are healed; and if anything comes in the end of healing, so you must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the iron band that we have spoken of before; and sometimes one administers a piece of cloth, and sometimes an appearance comes in the back part of the spine towards the back, and it is thought that it is a dislocation; and this is the bone that opens up, why one must not have presumption: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the thigh dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is known that the joints of the thigh and the shoulders do not dislocate other than in two parts, solely, and it does not come from them as from the other joints; and the joint of the thigh is dislocated in four parts: inward and outward, and front and back; and even more so, and frequently dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and there are more swollen veins on the patient's side than the healthy side, and the patient cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the spot which is near the inflamed abscess is hot.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who it comes out in front is that this accident is contrary to those in front. (This implies that the dislocation is on the opposite side of the body from where the knee joint is located.)
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who it comes out in front, are that his leg is well straightened according to the completion; however, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot move forward, and holds back his urine, and swells up his scrotum, and when he walks, he passes over his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who it comes out behind, are that he cannot stretch his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the scrotum is softened, and the tendons of the knee are at the same level as the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you return to the fact that the dislocation is ancient, and it stays in its position, so there is no cure; and it does not seem necessary to have hope. (This implies that if the dislocation has been present since childhood or a long time ago, it may be permanent and uncorrectable.)
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocation, you should hasten to turn the joint inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and there will be no need for further treatment. (This implies that if the dislocation is recent, it may be possible to treat it by manipulating the joint back into place.)
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, it is necessary that you apply the minister's force, and steady the leg strongly with both hands, or with one ligature tied over the knee; and another minister extends their hand above in such a manner that they pull their hands under his armpits, then tightens them with a single thread over the thigh; and another ties the chief of the ligature; and all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground to once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of stretching is common to all three appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well. (This implies that this treatment may be effective for a variety of different types or stages of dislocation.)
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, so it is necessary to apply treatment to its appearance When the dislocations are at the shoulder, so you must tie the patient on his healthy side, then put the ligature on the root of the scrotum, and the place that is below the armpit, then stretch the ligature up towards the armpit, and towards the navel; then take another servants arms, and enfold the thick part of the sick scrotum, and extend it outwards strongly: thus it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tie it in this manner that we have said, so you must tie the patient's two feet together with a strong soft ligature on both heels, and on both knees, and let the sick leg be extended two inches more than the others; then hang it up on a beam above the ground with two long ropes; then command one servant to enfold the head of the scrotum, and have another servant hanging with the patient, who enfold strongly the scrotum, for the joint returns now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in its final position, it lies down as we have said with gilbosity, and he has stretched on a leg bandage properly, and also on his back; then he puts two torches, one at the head and the other at the feet, then puts a torch between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and has wet cloths planted around him so that he does not hurt the patient, then stretches each attendant towards him, and the physician sets up equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	Then if not, place him on the bed, and press thus as we have said in the gilbosity, and has the patient lie on his right side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the ailing leg hastily and according to what I have said; and have the attendant place their hand on the ailing scrotum, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee. (This describes a more specific treatment for a front-facing dislocation.)
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in its final position, it does not need to extend the patient downward, nor lift him up on the ground, but rather he should be as if his hips were out of place in the end, as we have said about lying on two cushions; and he should lie on his back, and the ligatures should be extended as we have said before, and you must press upon the joint at the table; and it will be done when the patient stretches his legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply a poultice, and an elastic bandage, so that the hip does not move; and he should rest for three days or four, then release him, and put the poultice on him; and if you see that they are even, then bind him, as before, and leave him for three days; then release him, and make him walk slowly, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the knee dislocation.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated according to three manners: namely, inward and outward, and backward; and they do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And you command the patient to bend his leg to his knee, and if it does not stay in its place at the knee, know that it is dislocated. The restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on yours; then take his knee in your hands, and pull between your arms, and then bend both sides of the knee together; and another assistant stretches his foot, until the knee comes back to its place, and the sign is that it stays well in its place slightly; and apply the plaster on top, and make the leg stay at the knee, and bind them together tightly for three days or four, then loosen; and do not let the patient walk, until the member is comforted.

de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like you've switched to a new topic.

And when it is fixed in place, so put the poultice and stoppers on top, and the binding in place, and bind the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the bandage is not too tight; then let it be for 2 days or 3, and if the bandage loosens, tighten it again; then loosen it on the fourth day or the quarter, and forbid the patient from going out for 4 days; and if he goes before this time is up, it is not certain that it will not dislodge again.

des dois	It looks like we've reached the end of this medical text! "Des dois" means "of the feet" in French, which makes sense given the context of the previous paragraphs about treating an ankle injury. If you'd like to continue translating or have any further questions, feel free to ask!

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It looks like we've reached the end of this medical text! "De plaie et de dislocation ensamble" means "about wounds and dislocations together" in French, which suggests that the text has been treating both topics simultaneously. If you'd like to continue translating or have any further questions, feel free to ask!
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and we want to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor hard; use at first soothing remedies on a hot abscess, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset now the member to its place, so that the hot abscess comes; and when the member is back in place, administer soothing remedies for a hot abscess, and cure the wound, as it is fitting, with desiccating ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a breakage, and small bones are separated, then extract them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this will harm you according to your Creator, and because of the wisdom of arming yourself and your body.
